Business and Industrial Circles Feted Sun Tonggang Last Night 121

The business and industrial circles of this city held a banquet at the YMCA of the Eight Immortals Bridge last night at 7:00 pm to celebrate the return of young aviator Sun Tonggang. More than 50 people attended the banquet, including business and industrial leaders Wang Xiaolai, Zhu Xuefan, Lu Jingshi, Pan Xusheng, Zhou Xuexiang, Ye Jiaxing, Fei Yunqing, and representatives from various industries. Wang Xiaolai, chairman, gave a welcoming speech, and Sun Tonggang gave a reply. The chairman's welcoming speech and Sun's reply are recorded below.

Welcoming Speech: During the banquet, Chairman Wang Xiaolai gave a welcoming speech, saying: In the past, international wars were always decided by naval battles, so there was a saying that the sea dominates the land. In the future, wars may be decided by the air force, because the naval battles of the future must first use aircraft carriers to carry aircraft to determine the outcome of the air forces of both sides. If one side's air force is defeated, then the other side can arbitrarily bomb enemy ships and indicate the accurate distance for firing. Because the range of shells of modern warships is more than 10,000 meters, the distance is far, and it is not easy to hit the target without using the air force as eyes and ears. This is one reason. It is recently reported that the US naval strategy focuses on the air force and not on submarines, because when the air force drops bombs, it is not easy to identify them in the water, and there is a fear of accidentally injuring their own submarines. Therefore, the US circular formation tactics are purely to use the air force to control submarines. This is the second reason. In the future, the air force should be in the first place, which has become an indisputable conclusion. Therefore, what we require is that our country revitalize the air force, one is to improve the aviation technology, and the other is to popularize aviation schools. Mr. Tonggang drove his single-seater aircraft from Germany back to China, crossing the desert and experiencing climate changes and aircraft damage. He finally arrived safely in his motherland in a journey of more than 20 days. This kind of long-distance flight is common in foreign countries, but it is rare in our country. It is hoped that he can use his excellent technology to guide the younger generation and set an example for the whole country, so that those who have learned aviation knowledge should not be content with the status quo and stop after a little taste, and those who have not learned but have a healthy body should also sharpen their spirits and rush forward to regard this as an important plan to save the country and the people, so that talents will emerge in large numbers and be able to try it out when something happens. I have heard that during the European War, there were 5,000 German aviation personnel at the front and 5,000 undergoing training in the rear, and 758 were replenished to the front every month, which shows the urgent need for air force personnel in wartime. Therefore, what our country needs now is the improvement of technology and the universality of talents, and both should be given equal importance. It is hoped that Mr. Tonggang will lead in the front, and outstanding young people will respond in the rear, so that our nation will have a place to survive. In the past, people always regarded returning to their hometown with wealth as returning home in glory. This is too superficial. We believe that Mr. Tonggang must bring his national salvation knowledge and turn it into a national salvation career to be worthy of the name of returning in glory. Therefore, on the day of his departure from Shanghai, we gathered together to celebrate and express our admiration. I have also heard that Mr. Tonggang still plans to learn aircraft manufacturing technology in Germany. This is a heavy responsibility and a long road, and he does not limit himself to what he has learned, and he especially has the ancient style of patriotism. I wish him even greater progress and that he will make a major contribution to the country in the future and add a different color to the national history. The future is bright, and I hope he will cherish himself for the sake of the country.

Sun's Reply: Then, Mr. Sun Tonggang gave a reply, saying: Today, I am very grateful for the banquet and hospitality of the Shanghai business and industrial circles. I returned from Germany this year, and after returning to my hometown, I made a national flight, which took 57 days, flying for about 100 hours and traveling 14,000 miles. During the journey, I passed through the provinces of Hebei, Shanxi, Shaanxi, Henan, Hubei, etc., to Beijing. Wherever I went, I was warmly received, which shows that the people of the whole country have a deep interest in aviation. This time, I came here to accept the aircraft donated by Mr. Du, and I am very happy to meet with you all. There are three things that Tonggang can tell you: (1) Aircraft are not dangerous, (2) The flight time is very accurate, (3) Our country needs the development of the air force, and the most important thing is the cultivation of talents. This time, I heard in Shanghai that the China Aviation Association has a proposal to organize a flying club. Shanghai is the economic and political center of the country, and there must be such an organization to cultivate talents. I hope you will support it. At about 8:00, the guests and hosts enjoyed themselves and dispersed.

National Ships are Prohibited from Berthing at Fujian Ports, Effectively Blocking the Ports; Businessmen in Pingyang Stop Handling Goods 122

Ruian and Pingyang are border areas between Zhejiang and Fujian. Since the Fujian Incident occurred, the local situation has gradually become tight. Passenger and freight transportation has been suspended, and shipping has been blocked. The details are as follows:

Pingyang Stops Handling Goods: Pingyang, Zhejiang, borders Fujian. The main products of the area are coal and alum. Two companies in Shanghai, Huxing and Daxing, have a total of five ships operating. The area is a land port and goods are tax-free, so the export business of each ship is quite large. The main goods exported are northern and southern groceries and cloth. Since the Fujian Incident occurred, the trade between the area and Fuzhou has been cut off. Recently, due to the tense situation, the Pingyang businessmen have telegraphed Shanghai to stop handling goods. According to the two ship companies Daxing and Huxing, the Sanjiang ship will sail today, and there are no goods to be loaded in Shanghai, and the shipping business has suddenly become quiet.

Strict Local Defense: The Xin Sanjiang ship arrived in Shanghai from Pingyang yesterday. According to the ship's crew, since November 28, Pingyang has received Zhejiang troops dispatched by the central government, which have been transported from Wenzhou by small steamers in batches. They have been sent to the border with Fujian for defense. The central government's army is firmly defending the border between Fujian and Zhejiang, and the people in the Ruian and Pingyang areas have also stabilized. Although the freight volume of the Shanghai-Ruian ships has fallen sharply, the schedules are still open and have not been suspended.

Explicit Prohibition of Navigation in Fujian Waters: Yesterday, the Shanghai Shipping Administration Bureau issued Order No. 82 to various shipping companies, stating: Having received a telegram from Chairman Jiang of the Military Affairs Commission transferred by the Ministry of Communications, stating that since the Fujian Incident occurred, in addition to properly formulating countermeasures, please instruct the domestic commercial shipping companies not to berth at any ports along the coast of Fujian Province in order to cut off their water transportation and quell the rebellion as soon as possible. It is hoped that the handling situation will be telegraphed back. Upon receiving this, we must comply. In addition to telegraphing and distributing it, please inform all commercial shipping companies to abide by and report. The seal of the Ministry of Communications, etc. Yesterday, after the various shipping companies received this explicit order, they have informed the ship owners that if commercial ships pass along the coast of Fujian Province, they are not allowed to dock at any port in order to effectively block the Fujian waters.

Shanghai, Nanjing, and Jiangsu Tobacco and Alcohol Industry Representatives Petition in Beijing, Requesting Amendments to the New Tax Regulations, Accusing Tax Commissioner Xie Qi 126

The Joint Federation of Tobacco Industry Guilds of Shanghai, Nanjing, and Jiangsu, and the Joint Federation of Alcohol Industry Guilds, have repeatedly protested regarding the new tax regulations, all without result. Consequently, merchants and related workers in both industries feel extraordinarily pained. Therefore, eight representatives, including Yu Xunlu, Zhang Suhou, Zhang Dalian, and Chen Weiwen, were delegated to go to Beijing on the 25th to convene various representatives and discuss two concrete measures: (1) submitting a request to amend the tax regulations, and (2) accusing Tax Commissioner Xie Qi. On the 30th, they will go to the Executive Yuan, the Control Yuan, and the Ministry of Finance to petition and submit documents. The original text is recorded below:

Petition to the Government and Yuan: The purpose is to report that the Tax Commissioner has changed the old system and established new regulations, which harm businesses with excessive taxes. Enumerating the facts, we implore your Yuan to grant a consultation with the Ministry to dismiss him, to rectify matters, to emphasize national taxes, and to maintain people's livelihood. It has been found that Xie Qi, the Tax Commissioner of the Tax Bureau under the Ministry of Finance, has had some success in handling cigarette taxes and consolidated taxes, but he is unfamiliar with the situation of native tobacco and wine taxes. Moreover, native tobacco and wine have a considerable history, and local customs are uniquely different, relating to farmers' side businesses, and the nature of production and sales are completely different from cigarettes. Now, to have someone who has experience only in consolidated taxes but no experience in tobacco taxes take over this matter is already a misplacement of talent. Therefore, from the beginning of Commissioner Xie's takeover, he violated public opinion. The bidding contractor system for the tobacco and alcohol industries, which was hated like an enemy, had already been explicitly banned by the National Government. However, in the 21st year, the commissioner, under the beautiful name of the "Selection Committee System," was actually a disguised form of bidding contractors. All procedures were no different from bidding, causing fierce competition among general contractors, not only poisoning tobacco and alcohol merchants, but also making tax affairs extremely complicated. From then on, tax revenue was divergent, biased, and uneven. The rich left laughing with their pockets full, while the poor defaulted on public funds, abandoned their posts, and fled. The public sales achievements of previous years have all been swept away. A review of the original case of the 21st year's Selection Committee System will reveal its underlying secrets. The commissioner, fearing disregard for government orders and improper handling, and knowing that he could not escape blame, wanted to save the collapsing tide and cover up past mistakes. Thus, with wild ideas, he initiated further plans for special native tobacco taxes and fixed native wine taxes. If the plan were to succeed, all blame could be shifted to the poor public sales system. In reality, it smacked of recklessness, haste, and self-righteousness. It must be known that all political systems depend on human effort. If the public sales tax amount has been reformed over the past ten years, although it may not be perfect, it should not hinder national taxes, harm businesses, or sicken the people. Why abolish it so hastily? Prior consultations should have been broadly adopted. Why maintain strict secrecy? If Commissioner Xie truly had talent, knowing that the old system had drawbacks, he should have focused on eliminating accumulated malpractices. There was no need to change the course entirely. Simply remove the dross from the old system, retain its essence, and it would be enough. Only by increasing tax revenue, gradually eliminating embezzlement, benefiting the country above, and pacifying businesses below, could he be called a talented tax officer of the era. Now, the commissioner has taken over for two years and has already changed the system twice, even suggesting handling consolidated taxes in the same way as cigarettes. With such constantly changing orders, the people find it difficult to adapt. Now, this hybrid special native tobacco tax and fixed native wine tax have been recklessly set, completely ignoring the special circumstances of tobacco and alcohol, which relate to rural commerce and affect social peace. Is it possible that the national tax bureau does not have a single person familiar with the situation of tobacco and alcohol? This tax system can truly be called one of exorbitant taxes. Our Kuomintang's party platform has strictly prohibited this. Now, the various harassing articles are listed below: (1) Uneven tax rates. Examining the imitation Shaoxing wine (i.e., native yellow wine produced by Shaoxing merchants in Jiangsu), the tax rate for native yellow wine from various regions is 80 cents per 100 jin. However, the tax bureau cleverly created a name for native yellow wine produced by Shaoxing merchants in Jiangsu, calling it imitation Shaoxing wine, and taxing it at 1.40 yuan per 100 jin, an increase of 60 cents. For yellow wine brewed by Shaoxing merchants in various counties of Zhejiang province, the same tax is levied as for native yellow wine, without distinguishing the merchant's origin. Furthermore, the production area for Shaoxing wine is taxed at 1.40 yuan, while the sales area is taxed at 2 yuan. The taxes in the originating province should be equal, yet they are suddenly increased by 60 cents. However, native yellow wine produced by Jiangsu merchants has always been taxed equally, regardless of the merchant's origin (because the raw materials for Shaoxing merchants' yellow wine are indistinguishable from those of local yellow wine, and the selling price is similar). Equal treatment should be given to all. As for Shaoxing yellow wine, because it is produced in Shaoxing Prefecture and sold in other areas, the customary name is Shaoxing wine. Those sold within the former Shaoxing Prefecture are still called yellow wine. The tax bureau has set different tax rates for yellow wine produced in the former Shaoxing Prefecture of Zhejiang province: Shaoxing wine is taxed at 1.40 yuan per 100 jin, while yellow wine produced in other counties is called native yellow wine and taxed at 1 yuan per 100 jin. Moreover, Shaoxing wine has always been subject to provincial tax surcharges in the production area, amounting to 86.4 cents per 100 jin and a public treasury fee of 80 cents, totaling 1.664 yuan. When Jiangsu province abolished the likin tax, the provincial tax had already been abolished. Only a public sales fee was levied, at 1.20 yuan per 100 jin. Merchants acknowledged this, and the actual payment was 76.8 cents per 100 jin. Now, with the new system, according to the original public sales fee value of 20%, why is Shaoxing wine suddenly increased to 2 yuan per 100 jin? The actual tax rate is increased by 1.232 yuan. It is self-evident that the sales area is taxed more heavily than the production area. Also, in Shanghai, native yellow wine has traditionally been untaxed in the concessions and taxed at half rate in the Chinese area (i.e., special treatment). Now, the new system has failed to implement taxation in the concessions but has suddenly abolished the half rate and retroactively levied the full tax in the Chinese area. The above three points are clear evidence of uneven tax rates. (2) Extortion along the way. In the past, during the public sales period, merchants only needed to pay taxes to transport tobacco and alcohol without obstruction. Now, with the implementation of the new system, even after paying taxes and obtaining certificates, inspections are conducted along the way. The inspection procedures resemble disguised likin taxes. Furthermore, all kinds of difficulties are created, and payments must be made before passage is allowed. For example, 69 pieces of tobacco leaves from Jiangyin were extorted at 10 cents per piece when passing through Suzhou and Wuxi, amounting to 6.9 yuan. Another example is 15 years' worth of tobacco leaves from Guanyun, which were extorted at 1 yuan per piece by the Guantonggan sub-bureau, amounting to 15 yuan. (Both of these cases have been telegraphed to the Jiangsu Provincial Bureau by the association for investigation.) Furthermore, four boats of Zhang Kelai wine from Taixing, passing through Hengtang Town in Suzhou and Wuxi, had already paid taxes and affixed certificates according to regulations. However, the patrol boat inspector falsely claimed that the tax was insufficient and forcibly demanded a huge tax supplement of 200 dan, threatening a fine of 5,000 yuan. In reality, they wanted to extort fees for the certificate. The merchant requested an inspection by opening the jars and verifying the quantity and tax amount, which were found to be in compliance. They should have been released, but the inspector, failing to extort money, falsely accused the merchant of assaulting the inspector and sent the merchant to the local public security bureau, detaining him for five days. The above three points are clear evidence of extortion along the way. (3) Excessive penalties. When Taixing wine was transported to Shanghai, the public fee was previously calculated at 58% of the value. This time, with the new system, the sub-bureau stipulated that it should be calculated at 75% including the skin, according to regulations. However, the inspection office re-inspected and deemed it non-compliant, forcibly calculating it at 80%, and considering the remaining forty-odd dan as deliberate tax evasion by the wine merchant, rendering the affixed tax certificates completely invalid, re-levying the tax, confiscating the wine, and imposing a fine of more than five times the amount. This is clear evidence of excessive penalties. (4) Resembling double taxation. The government has explicitly ordered one tax per item. Tobacco and alcohol inventories have already paid the public treasury fee tax. Of course, the goods have already been taxed. Even if new regulations are revised, there is no reason for double taxation. As in the past, when the likin tax was abolished and replaced with a unified tax, items such as flour, yarn, cement, and matches were subject to the unified tax. We have not seen shops being refunded the old tax and required to pay the new tax. Now, for the tobacco and alcohol industries, shops are ordered to refund the old and pay the new, which is no different from double taxation. Moreover, for the inventories of retail shops, since they have already paid the public sales fee tax, there should be no need for registration (as exemplified by the Shanghai soy sauce and wine industry's request to be exempt from supplementing the new tax). Otherwise, it resembles double taxation. (5) Discriminatory treatment. While the fixed native wine tax is divided into categories with different tax rates, the special native tobacco leaf tax does not differentiate between high and low grades. All are taxed at 4.15 yuan per 100 jin. For high-grade tobacco leaves worth 70-80 yuan, the tax is 4.15 yuan, while for low-grade tobacco leaves worth 2-3 yuan, the tax is also 4.15 yuan. The cost difference is like heaven and earth. Tax rates should be differentiated according to the quality, as with wine. Otherwise, it is clear evidence of discriminatory treatment. In summary, the above points show that harassment has become a reality. Moreover, old habits have not been eliminated, and new problems are emerging. They claim that the laws are good and the intentions are beautiful, with no harm and only benefits. However, after the reform, tobacco and alcohol tax revenue has sharply declined compared to before. The underlying reason is the commissioner's poor implementation. Therefore, at the beginning of the implementation, he used collusion tactics, appointing Huang Yuming (i.e., Huang Lu), the executive committee member of the association, as the director of the Shanghai Public Treasury Sub-bureau, making him a henchman to strictly oppress the people. Unexpectedly, the people's hearts have not died, and justice still exists. The sub-bureau director handled matters for three months with no results, and he retired in shame. For months, tax officials and merchants were in distress. It should be known that merchants are willing to accept tax increases by the government and fulfill their obligations, bearing the pain. There is no reason to resist, as long as the tax rates are fair and the procedures are convenient. Now, the commissioner is biased, holding prejudices and hating merchants. What crime have the merchants committed to suffer such misery? The associations, on behalf of all tobacco and alcohol merchants in Shanghai, Nanjing, and Jiangsu, have specially delegated representatives to enumerate the facts and submit a document requesting your Yuan to review and promptly consult with the Ministry to dismiss and punish him, to emphasize national taxes and maintain people's livelihood. We are infinitely grateful. In addition to submitting to (Executive Yuan), (Control Yuan), and the Ministry of Finance, we respectfully submit to the National Government (Chairman Yu of the Control Yuan) and (Chairman Wang of the Executive Yuan). Yu Xunlu, Chairman of the Joint Federation of Shanghai, Nanjing, and Jiangsu Alcohol Industry Guilds, Standing Committee Members Zhang Suhou, Cao Gexian, Xu Songji, Yao Jiansan. Zhang Dalian, Chairman of the Joint Federation of Shanghai, Nanjing, and Jiangsu Tobacco Industry Guilds, Standing Committee Members Jin Yunjie, Dai Zhuoan, Jin Jiayue, Chen Weiwen.

Postponement of Shanghai-Tongguan Freight Train Service 127

The Shanghai-Nanjing, Tianjin-Pukou, and Longhai Railway Bureaus previously received an order from the Ministry of Railways to prepare for a Shanghai-Tongguan freight train service, running once daily from Shanghai Station on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway and Tongguan Station on the Longhai Railway, passing through the Tianjin-Pukou Railway. However, after the implementation of the direct Shanghai-Pingjin through freight train service, goods transported from Tongguan to Shanghai are now transported via the Longhai Railway to Xuzhou Station, where they are transferred to the Shanghai-Pingjin freight train to Shanghai. Similarly, goods transported from Shanghai to Tongguan can be loaded onto the Shanghai-Pingjin freight train to Xuzhou Station and then unloaded and loaded onto the Longhai Railway freight train to Tongguan. Therefore, the Shanghai-Tongguan freight train service is temporarily unnecessary and has been postponed. The rumor that the Shanghai-Tongguan through transport would begin today is incorrect, as the national railway through transport has been implemented since November 1st.

All airmail to Xinjiang currently held at the Hami post office awaiting dispatch will be forwarded to their destinations on the day the airmail service between Hami and Dihua resumes, and transit will still be rapid.

Altered and Defaced Banknotes Indistinguishable from Genuine Notes - Society Suffers Significantly, Witnesses Also Apprehended 133

Detectives Wang Chengying, Yang Xiguang, Yan Huang, Wang Hongsheng, and Liu Zhongcheng of the Jiaxing Road police station, learned that at No. 32 North Zhejiang Road and No. 231 Keenleah Road, someone was specializing in altering invalid banknotes from the closed Zhili and Guangdong Provincial Banks to resemble banknotes from the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Zhongnan Bank, Ningbo Commercial Bank, and Agricultural and Industrial Bank, and passing them off as genuine notes in the market. Countless people have been deceived. Thus, at around 1 AM the day before yesterday, they secretly went to the addresses and apprehended the ringleader, Zhu Zhixiang from Zhenjiang, Zhu Likang, and a woman Zhu Zhang (i.e., Zhu Zhixiang's wife). Zhu Zhang was hiding on the rooftop of No. 32 North Zhejiang Road, but was still arrested. Zhu Zhang was responsible for altering the banknotes and sending them to various places for sale. 140 Zhili and Guangdong scrapped notes and altered notes totaling 228 yuan, along with eleven forged seals of various banks, inks, account books, knives, and other items were seized. Zhu Shouying and Zhang Yutang from Yangzhou, were also taken into custody as suspects, and separately detained. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The police station's lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, stated the previous events, and stated that the defendants' method of alteration was to first use a knife to scrape off the words "Zhili" and "Guangdong". The three sizes of the various bank seals were used to change the value: the large seals to ten yuan, the medium to five yuan, and the small to one yuan, because the scrapped notes were originally one yuan each. After altering the Chinese and Western text, the notes were placed in a book overnight, and the alterations were undetectable, looking no different from the genuine notes. These people's skills were sophisticated, no different than a real note, and society has suffered greatly. He then submitted the notes and evidence for inspection. When questioned, Zhu Zhixiang confessed that this type of business began in March of this year, and a total of about four to five hundred yuan had been altered. The sources were purchased from money shops and tea servers, with minimal profit. Zhu Zhang denied the responsibility of selling the forged notes. Zhu Likang stated that he was staying at his friend Ni Haiming's attic at 231 Keenleah Road, and was not involved in this case. The police station's lawyer Zhang stated that the rent for the attic was found to have been paid by him, and 40 scrapped notes were also seized, indicating that the two parties were indeed in contact. When questioned, Zhu Shouying and Zhang Yutang stated that they had recently come to Shanghai from their hometown to sell chickens and crabs, and were staying at Zhu Zhixiang's place on North Zhejiang Road. The rest of the statements were evasive. Judge Xiao Xiefen ordered them to be remanded to custody separately and rescheduled for further investigation and verification.

Cricket Gambling Case Tried - Defendants Released on Bail Who Appeared Were Punished Yesterday - Defendants Who Did Not Appear Will Be Strictly Summoned Again for Interrogation 134

The building at No. 90 Jingxing Lane, Ningbo Road, owned by Huaan Bank, is actually owned by Wing Hang Bank. Regulations on Installation and Rental Fees 137

(A) Wall-mounted phone: Deposit fee of 50 yuan, installation fee of 20 yuan, monthly rental fee: Category A, 7 yuan; Category B, 10 yuan. (B) Desk phone: Deposit fee of 50 yuan, installation fee of 20 yuan, monthly rental fee: Category A, 8 yuan; Category B, 11 yuan. (C) Extension phone: Deposit fee of 50 yuan, installation fee of 10 yuan, monthly rental fee: Category A, 3 yuan; Category B, 3 yuan. Also, the number of calls between Pudong users and the Concession is temporarily set as follows: (1) Residential users: The monthly average should not exceed 40 calls. (2) Business users: Should not exceed 80 calls. The standard for the number of calls is calculated from the start of the call between the two parties, with every three minutes counting as one time (even if less than three minutes, it is calculated as one time). Each call costs 5 cents. If the call time exceeds three minutes, it is counted as two times. If it exceeds six minutes, it is counted as three times, and so on. The excess call fee will be notified to the users by the bureau on a monthly basis, and then collectors will be sent to collect the fees from the users with receipts. The amount will be included in the monthly rental fee bill.

The National Cotton Yarn Association Held its Second General Meeting Yesterday; Amended Articles of Association Passed, Eight Important Proposals Approved; Discussions and Election of Officers to Continue Today 141

Wu Liande Speaks on the Characteristics of the Chinese and English Nationalities 142

At noon on November 26th, the Returned Students Association held a luncheon at the Cathay Hotel, specially inviting Dr. Wu Liande to give a lecture entitled "The Characteristics of the Chinese and English Nationalities." Dr. Wu is an authority on public health, renowned both domestically and internationally. In this lecture, he meticulously explored the characteristics of the Chinese and English nationalities, presenting incisive arguments. The audience responded with thunderous applause. The following is a summary of Dr. Wu's speech:

The characteristics of a nationality, apart from heredity, are entirely determined by its environment. Therefore, to understand the evolution of a nationality, one must first examine the conditions of its origins. People often mistakenly believe that the purer the race, the stronger it is, such as the English, whose race is the purest, and therefore the most prosperous nation in the world. In fact, this is a great misconception. Now, please allow me to quote the words of former British Prime Minister Baldwin. Baldwin said that England was once under the rule of the great Roman Empire, so it became stained with a kind of aristocratic flavor. It was then conquered by the Saxons, a cruel and fierce race, which added a grain of seasoning. Later, various Nordic peoples mixed in, indirectly resulting in the ancestors who opened up England. Finally, they were conquered by the Norman people, becoming a mixture of Nordic and French races. Their sense of unity and national concept also became apparent. The reason why today's English people are rich in a spirit of cooperation, have a deep sense of family, possess a humorous flavor, and are able to dominate the seas and emigrate all over the world is because they are a mixed race.

Our Chinese people often have a misunderstanding about mixed races. Since the discovery of the "Peking Man" remains in Zhoukoudian near Beijing, it can perhaps be regarded as the ancestor of mankind. Leaving this aside for the moment, what can now be asserted is that the base of our Han nationality was in the provinces of Shaanxi and Henan, about 5,000 years ago, and then gradually advanced north and south. The reason why the people of Guangdong Province in our country have an adventurous spirit and an enterprising spirit is because their race is extremely mixed, containing a mixture of the earliest immigrants, Hakka, Dutch, Arab, Malay, Dutch, and Caucasian. Their descendants are also almost all over the world, such as Annam, Malaysia, the Dutch East Indies, Australia, Canada, Hawaii, the Philippines, the United States, Nikolayevsk, and other places, all have Guangdong immigrants. For example, in Hong Kong, the backbone of its society is a mixed race of Cantonese and English people. Furthermore, the founders of the three major department stores in Hong Kong, Guangzhou, and Shanghai are all mixed-race overseas Chinese from Australia.

If we take a look at our country's history, when China was invaded by the Mongol, Hun, and Manchu nationalities, because the Han culture and unity were higher than the invading nationalities, they gradually became assimilated, and the inferior nature of the nomadic peoples was also absorbed at the same time. However, it was not like the English, who were able to fully absorb the superior qualities of the Roman, Saxon, and Norman peoples. Therefore, today's Chinese nationality lacks unity, excessively develops harmful selfishness, and has no scientific spirit. The reason for this is that the absorption of the inferior nature of the Manchus and Mongols has dragged down evolution.

Dr. Wu continued, saying that if you want to study history or the characteristics of a certain nationality, you must refer to anecdotal texts, especially biographies and novels. For example, by reading Scott's novels, you can know the truth about Scotland. If you want to know English life, it is best to browse Dickens's and Thackeray's works. The characteristics of our Chinese people can also be found in novels, such as Luo Guanzhong's Romance of the Three Kingdoms, which is particularly outstanding in its depiction of national character.

Dr. Wu concluded by saying that China and England have quite a few similar characteristics. Both have a glorious history, are rich in conservatism and enterprising spirit, have commercial solidarity, and treat foreign nationalities well (for example, China is the only country that has never expelled Jews, but instead assimilated them). Therefore, the two countries have common points and have close ties. They should learn from each other's strengths and make up for each other's weaknesses. Finally, he quoted the words of the former British ambassador to China, Lampson, at a farewell banquet in Beijing, "The two great nations of China and England have many similarities. Both are rich in basic common sense and have a keen ability to coordinate. What is beneficial to one country must also be beneficial to the other. I hope that this will lead to further understanding."

Private Shipping Companies' Request to Participate in Joint Transportation Resolved; Joint Office Established to Implement Cooperation; Private Companies to be Invited to Discuss Solutions 143

The state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (招商局) is managing the national water and land joint transportation. Various private shipping companies united to fight for permission to join. Therefore, this dispute has been completely resolved. The details are recorded below:

(Solution): According to the New Voice News Agency's Beijing correspondent, Liu Hongsheng, general manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, came to Beijing the day before yesterday and jointly consulted with Yu Tan, director of the Business Department of the Ministry of Railways, Assistant Tan Yaozong, Yang Xianfen, deputy director of the Joint Transportation Office, and Gao Tingzi, director of the Shipping Administration Department of the Ministry of Communications, on the method of responsible joint water and land transportation. At that time, they all believed that private shipping is also providing services to society, and their request to participate is justified. However, the private shipping companies have different capital, routes, ships, docks, and warehouses. To facilitate the process, it was agreed that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Sanbei Company would first convene various private shipping companies to discuss the method and establish a joint organization, named the Joint Office of Private and State-run Shipping Companies. Those who wish to participate in responsible water and land joint transportation must have definite routes, docks, and warehouses before November 1, and have registered with the Shipping Administration Department of the Ministry of Communications and filed with the Ministry of Industry. They may apply to the two ministries of communications and railways for participation, and then discuss with each other in the joint office the method of jointly undertaking the transportation of goods. In this way, all railway freight in the country that requires water and land joint transportation to reach the final destination can be fully realized by the Joint Transportation Office and the Joint Office negotiating and signing a contract. As for the future negotiation of this contract, it will still be based on the contract signed between the China Merchants Steam Navigation

The Hongzhen Bloodshed Incident: Shen Linghua Dies, Du Linsheng Injured 144

Shen Jinhua, a local resident, 40 years old, a coppersmith, and his younger brother, Shen Linghua, 34 years old, a tailor, both married with children, lived together at No. 21 Dong Yaojia Stone Bridge, Hongzhen, Zhabei. The family also has an elderly mother, who is over seventy years old. Usually, the two brothers work independently and live frugally, so although they cannot live in luxury, they are still well-fed. Shen Linghua also has a tailor shop at home, employing many tailors, who work all day long. Because the weather has turned cold recently, the work has been more frequent, so Shen and his employees, including Du Linsheng, work day and night, not sleeping until late at night. At about 2:00 AM yesterday morning, Shen Du and others thought it was late, so they stopped working and went to bed. Not long after, they suddenly heard a very urgent knock on the door. At that time, Du Linsheng had not yet fallen asleep, so he planned to get up and unlock the door, but the door had already been broken down by the people outside the door. When Du stepped off the bed, the crowd had already rushed in. Seeing Du Linsheng, they did not ask why, and stabbed him all over with sharp blades, causing him to be covered in wounds and lying in a pool of blood. Seeing that their goal had been achieved, the murderers fled in droves. However, Du was still conscious and desperately cried for help, alarming Shen Linghua and others upstairs. They put on their clothes and went downstairs to investigate. Seeing this situation, Shen rushed out of the house and searched for the whereabouts of the murderers. But when he reached a wasteland called Baiyangtan nearby, a person suddenly jumped out from the side of the road and chopped Shen with an axe. Because the disaster happened suddenly, Shen could not avoid it and was killed on the spot. Shen's brother, Jinhua, was unable to rescue him, so he quickly woke up Wang Shiyi, Shen Hongqing, Wang Asheng, and others who lived together, and first sent Du Linsheng to the hospital for treatment. On the way, they met a patrol of Chinese policemen from the Yulin Road police station. After questioning, because the matter was related to assassination, they were taken to the police station for filing and then sent to Sacred Heart Hospital in Yangshupu for treatment. Shen Linghua's body was later reported to the Fifth District, Third Precinct by Shen Jinhua, who instructed the local landlord to report to the court for inspection. The precinct also sent police to investigate the scene and summoned Shen Jinhua and others to the precinct for questioning, and dispatched detectives to search for the murderers everywhere. As for the cause of the incident, it is said that it was caused by a love rivalry.

Company and the Joint Transportation Office. The general outline will not change much. If there are any losses in the freight, the Joint Office will be responsible for compensation.

Bandits Disturbing Yangtze River Ships; Military Commission Takes Action to Suppress and Maintain Order; Gospel for Yangtze River Travelers; Prohibiting Bandits from Impersonating Soldiers; New Prohibition Order Announced Today 145

Recently, Yangtze River ships have been disturbed by roving soldiers and coolies, making it impossible for passengers to travel by ship. When Mr. Xu of the Central Party Headquarters went to Jiangxi, he witnessed this and deeply believed that unless strict measures are taken, no one will take the Yangtze River national ships. Therefore, he discussed with the Military Commission to reorganize the Yangtze River ships. This matter is of great importance to the shipping industry, and the following is a report:

Disturbing National Ships: Recently, Yangtze River national ships, whether going up or down the river, from Zhenjiang to Jiujiang, have been almost always occupied by large numbers of roving soldiers, scattered soldiers, and coolies. These lost coolies, whether genuine or fake, are indistinguishable. After boarding the ship, they do not ask about the situation and forcibly occupy the cabins. Even if there are passengers inside, they forcibly order them to give way. Disputes and arguments are almost inevitable on every ship. This time, when the Jianguo ship returned to Shanghai from Hankou, the traffic on the ship was blocked by soldiers and coolies, and the crew could hardly cope with it.

Party Committee Witnessed: Mr. Xu, a member of the Nanjing Central Executive Committee, went to Xunyang on official business this time. He boarded a Yangtze River ship in Nanjing and traveled upstream. After boarding the ship, he witnessed soldiers and coolies boarding the ship everywhere along the way, causing all kinds of disturbances to public order, which cannot be enumerated. Mr. Xu investigated in detail and found that most of the roving soldiers and coolies were bandits from various places impersonating them. Therefore, he decided to report this situation to the Military Affairs Commission and take strict measures to maintain the operation of the Yangtze River ships.

Approved by the Military Commission: After Mr. Xu arrived in Jiujiang, he reported this matter to the Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, who decided to investigate and deal with it. Now, this case has been taken over by the Military Commission, and the first step is to conduct a thorough investigation to find out whether all the disruptive elements on the Yangtze River ships are impersonating them. The Military Commission has appointed secret investigators for this purpose and issued special symbols. They will go to various Yangtze River ships and ride back and forth to investigate the bandits impersonating them and severely punish them to ensure the safety of travelers.

Three-Month Period: The secret investigation period has been tentatively set for three months. The Military Commission and the various shipping companies in this port have agreed that it will be implemented from December 1. The companies will notify each Yangtze River ship to check the credentials of the assigned personnel and exempt them from ship tickets. The companies will not pay them salaries but only provide food. It is said that the aim of the secret investigators is to reorganize the bandits and fake soldiers along the river who are harmful to travelers. Therefore, when they board the ship to carry out their inspection tasks, they are similar to ordinary passengers, making it impossible for people to recognize them.

Promulgation of Measures: At the same time, the Military Commission also formulated regulations restricting military personnel from taking ships and ordered various military organs and commercial shipping companies to post them on various Yangtze River ships and implement them from today. The measures are roughly as follows: (1) Military officers of all levels who take ships with formal certificates and symbols can take first-class cabins and officer cabins and pay half the ticket price. (2) Formal troops of one platoon or more (45 people) taking Yangtze River ships will be charged 50 cents per person according to special measures. (3) If they are traveling from Yichang in the upper reaches of the river to various ports in Gan, Anhui, and Su, they will be charged one yuan per person. (4) If they are demobilized soldiers returning to various places with certificates, the ship ticket will be waived, and they will pay for their own food. (5) For the transportation of military supplies and ordnance, those with formal passports will pay half the freight. In addition, if there are those who do not comply with the regulations or forcibly take ships by impersonating military personnel, the ships may hand them over to the nearest military and police organs for severe punishment to enforce discipline and maintain shipping.

Ship Collision Committee Resolved Collision Case at Yesterday's Meeting 146

The Shanghai Shipping Administration Bureau's Ship Collision Dispute Resolution Committee held its fifth meeting at 9:00 AM yesterday. The committee members present were Sha Huijia, Xu Zufan, Yu Shifan, Chen Zhuzun, Chen Ganqing, etc. The chairman was Zhu Yaoting, and the recorder was Zhu Guanying. They discussed: (1) the case of the Runhua ship of the Ping An Shipping Company colliding with the No. 1 ship of the Daxing Shipping Company in Chongming Beisha. It was resolved to inquire about the collision situation from the captain of the Daxing Shipping Company and then discuss it again. (2) the case of the Fuxing ship of the Daxing Shipping Company colliding with the Dahua ship of the Ping An Shipping Company in the Huangpu River. It was resolved that the Dahua Shipping Company would bear all the losses of the Fuxing ship. (3) the case of the Fengxiang ship of the Taifeng Shipping Company colliding with the Dian ship of the Zhengji Shipping Company in the Huangpu River. It was resolved that the Fengxiang would bear 80% of the fault and the Dian ship would bear 20%. The meeting adjourned at 11:00 AM.

Commercial Inspection Bureau Sends Personnel to Huizhou to Promote the Ban on Colored Tea 152

The green tea produced in the Anhui and Zhejiang areas of our country is of excellent quality and has always been favored by foreigners. In recent years, the coloring of tea leaves has often contained inferior impurities, which has led to unfavorable publicity by Indian and Japanese tea merchants, and consumer countries have refused to import them, which has greatly affected international trade. The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, in view of this, has submitted a proposal to the Ministry of Industry to prohibit the export of colored tea. Although it is temporarily allowed to be handled this year, the ban will be strictly enforced from the time the new tea is on the market next year. However, the coloring of Chinese tea has been a long-standing practice, and it is difficult to completely eliminate it in a short period of time. To implement it, there must be sufficient preparation. On the one hand, tea merchants should be made aware of the importance of prohibiting the export of colored tea, and on the other hand, non-toxic coloring materials should be temporarily provided for substitution. The bureau has conducted various experiments and formulated various non-toxic coloring materials, which have been issued to Chinese and foreign tea merchants in Shanghai for trial use, and they have all been satisfied. Now, it is submitting a request to the Ministry of Industry for approval and limiting Chinese and foreign tea merchants to use them uniformly. It is deeply feared that the inland does not know the truth, so it has entrusted Mr. Fu Hongzhen, a technician from the Qimen Tea Improvement Farm, to take the opportunity to conduct detailed publicity on the ban on colored tea while investigating tea leaves in various parts of Huizhou. If it is unavoidable in the future, tea must be colored, and this non-toxic alternative coloring material should be used to improve tea leaves and consider the business situation of both parties.

Ministry of Education to Hire Committee Members to Draft Standard Teacher Training Curriculum 156

Since the Ministry of Education has not yet formulated curriculum standards for teacher training schools, it had previously hired committee members to organize a discussion group on teaching subjects in teacher training schools. After several days of meetings, the group agreed on a table of teaching subject hours for various types of teacher training, which was approved and promulgated by the Ministry of Education and ordered to be implemented. This was the first step. The second step is to hire another group of committee members to draft curriculum standards for various courses in various types of teacher training schools, so that each can draft curriculum standards for the subjects they are responsible for. It is reported that the number of committee members to be hired this time will be much larger, about eighty or ninety people, due to the large number of subjects, unlike the twenty or so members of the textbook discussion committee. Therefore, a meeting will not be convened for the time being. After the drafting is roughly completed in the future, small group meetings will be held for each subject separately. The selection of committee members for this meeting has been largely determined and will be announced soon. After the teacher training curriculum standards are formulated, teacher training schools can also hold joint entrance examinations in accordance with secondary schools. It is also reported that the Ministry of Education will revise the measures for joint entrance examinations for primary and secondary schools soon. In the future, primary schools can be exempted from joint entrance examinations, and provincial and municipal educational administrative authorities will formulate random examination measures.

Educational Film International Circulation Convention: Chinese Representative Proposes Amendment 161

In order to promote educational films, the International Federation, through the International Educational Film Association, drafted a draft convention to facilitate the circulation of educational films, and convened an international conference in Geneva last month. The Chinese representatives attending the conference were Hu Shize, the Chinese Minister to Switzerland, and Luo Shian, the secretary of the Chinese delegation to the League of Nations. They proposed the following amendment to Article 3 of the convention: "If a contracting party believes that a film licensed by the International Educational Film Association does not conform to the spirit and items of Article 1, it may state the reasons and request a re-examination. If the Association considers the reasons sufficient, it will revoke the license." This was well received by the representatives of various countries. In this way, films that are considered non-compliant can be fundamentally banned. In addition, the international conference discussed the text for two weeks, and both Hu and Luo worked extremely hard.

Overview of the Chinese College of the University of Paris (Part Two) 164

(2) Administration: Article 5 of the charter of the Chinese College stipulates that the college shall be managed by a council (also known as a supervisory meeting). The council members are the Dean of the French Academy, the President of the University of Paris, the President of Peking University, one representative of the Chinese government, two representatives of the Council of the University of Paris, and nine council members elected by the General Assembly of the College (four French and five Chinese). A Board of Directors is also established by the Council, which consists of one French Chairman, two Chinese and French Vice-Chairmen each, one Chinese and French Secretary each, and one French Accountant. In fact, the Council currently has only ten members, whose names and qualifications are as follows: 1. French side: Mr. Ban Lewei, Chairman; Mr. Mo Ni, Accountant; Mr. Keluozi, Dean of the French Academy; Mr. Shagedi, President of the University of Paris; Mr. Gewacai, Director of the French Academy; Mr. Bao Hai, Representative of the Council of the University of Paris; Mr. Telushe, same as above; Mr. Boshhe, Professor of the French Academy; Mr. Buwaye, President of the Paris Oriental Language School; 2. Chinese side: Mr. Li Shizeng, Representative of the Chinese government. From 1929 to 1931, the Ministry of Education hired former Chinese Minister to France, Mr. Gao Shuqing, as the acting representative. Since Mr. Gao returned to China in the winter of 1931, Mr. Liu Hou has been hired as the acting representative (before 1929, the representative of the Chinese government was Mr. Han Rujia). Mr. Xu Shichang, Mr. Wang Jingwei, Mr. Ye Gongchuo. The internal administration of the Chinese College is managed by one Director, who is Professor Gelanye of the College, and one Secretary, who is Mr. Mo Si. Both can attend the Council meetings, but have no voting rights. In terms of research, there is a research guidance committee, composed of seven Sinologists: Boshhe, Gelanye, Masbaiyi, Nalewa, Hakan, Feiluo, and Buwaye.

(3) Curriculum: Before 1926, the Chinese College was unable to develop due to economic difficulties. It only gave public lectures on Chinese culture in the classrooms of the Oriental Language School or the University of Paris every year. It officially started classes in the spring of 1927, offering seven lectureships:

(1) Chinese Culture, Professor Gelanye, Local Customs, etc.

(2) Chinese Literature, Linguistics, and Art, Professor Boshhe, Sinology, Painting, etc.

(3) Chinese Aesthetics, Lecturer Nalewa, Poetry, etc.

(4) Modern Chinese Political and Diplomatic History, Lecturer Dibabiyie, the influence of foreign powers on Chinese internal affairs and the Mongolian issue.

(5) Modern and Contemporary Chinese Economic History, Lecturer Mo Si, Research on Xu Guangqi's Complete Book of Agricultural Administration.

(6) Chinese Law, Lecturer Aisi Jiawa, Interpretation of Han Feizi, etc.

(7) Chinese Science, stipulated to hire Chinese people, regardless of any kind of science.

The above six lectureships all have full-time teachers, but it is extremely difficult to hire a professor for the Chinese Science lectureship. It is not easy for those who study Chinese science to come to Europe, or they are limited by language and cannot give lectures. Those who study science in Europe have not seen Chinese science before. Therefore, the Chinese Science lectureship has not yet been filled. Four years ago, Mr. Sheng Cheng lectured on Chinese sericulture. The following year, Mr. Shang Ping was hired to lecture on Chinese agriculture and special products. The following year, Mr. Chu Minyi lectured on Chinese medicine. Last year, because there were no suitable Chinese scientists in Europe, the lectureship was temporarily changed to Chinese Literature, and Mr. Zhang Fengju was in charge. It has been decided that Mr. Wu Kang, Dean of the Faculty of Arts of Sun Yat-sen University, will come to France to teach literature next year.

In addition to these seven lectureships, there are experts who are temporarily invited to lecture on certain special issues, such as Demieville lecturing on Tang Dynasty Buddhism, Favre lecturing on various secret societies in China, Dr. Leger lecturing on Chinese epidemics and hygiene, Masbaiyi lecturing on Taoism before the Tang Dynasty, and Dubosg lecturing on the current situation in China. Chen Mian also gave a lecture on Chinese opera.

The professors hired by the Chinese College, except for Gelanye and Boshhe, who are famous Sinologists, such as Dibabiyie and Dibuske, lectured on very superficial topics, mostly excerpted from ordinary newspapers and magazines, not specialized research. However, there are very few Europeans who understand Chinese, and it is very difficult to hire suitable people. This is also something that cannot be helped.

(4) Students and Their Grades: The number of students at the Chinese College has gradually increased in the past four years. There were 17 students in 1930, 27 in 1931, 39 in 1932, and 36 this year. By nationality, this year there are 18 Chinese, 12 French, and one each from Annam, Belgium, Germany, Japan, England, and Russia. The academic grades of the college are divided into certificates and diplomas. Students who study for one year and pass the exam are given a certificate. Students who study for two years, pass the exam, and submit a short thesis are given a diploma. However, to date, only one person from Poland and one person from Annam have passed the exam and obtained a diploma. Only one Russian female student and one French female student have obtained a certificate. Most of the Chinese students who attend classes at the college are preparing a thesis at the University of Paris and have already obtained a doctorate in liberal arts, totaling eleven people.

Municipal Education Bureau Rectifies Private Schools 168

The Municipal Education Bureau, in view of the large number of private tutoring schools, correspondence schools, and vocational training centers in the city, believes that those who can strictly abide by the education laws and regulations and apply to the bureau for establishment and registration are in an endless stream. However, there are still unscrupulous people who use the name of schools to post enrollment advertisements in order to achieve their purpose of defrauding money, causing young students to often not understand the actual situation, be deceived and harmed by them. There have been several cases of complaints to the bureau, especially from remote areas. Now, in addition to carefully investigating and strictly banning bad schools, the bureau has also sent letters to various newspapers, ordering them to indicate the words "established or registered with the approval of the Municipal Education Bureau" on all private school advertisements from now on. Otherwise, they will not be published. It has also ordered private schools that have been approved for establishment and registration to comply with this.

Jinan Suffers a Crushing Defeat of 5-1: Luo Haiguang Not as Steady as He Used to Be, Xu Yahui Unable to Support the Entire Edifice Alone 177

Jinan had previously fought against Huosais twice, with the players giving their all. Fortunately, both matches ended in a 1-1 draw. Yesterday was their second encounter in the Schicota Cup. The Huo team's skills have been improving daily. The entire match yesterday was tense, and their footwork was also very nimble. In the morning, they took the lead with a score of 2-1. Near the end of the afternoon session, they launched a sudden attack, scoring three consecutive goals. Among Jinan's forwards, only Yahui was seen actively contributing. Center-back Xiaoyun was also quite competent. Gu Shangxiang and Xu Heng's contributions were balanced, with no major gains or losses.

First Half Saw Give-and-Take Exchanges: After lining up, the fierce battle began. Both sides immediately adopted an absolute offensive posture, resulting in a chaotic scene on the field, with players running and kicking intensely. The Huo team's five forwards repeatedly probed the goal, but all were blocked by Xu Heng. Xuebaite gained possession and moved north, breaking through the center-back line, delivering a perfectly placed cross to the center. Xu Heng missed the save, and Kangmuden tapped the ball into the goal. Jinan then launched a full-scale counterattack. Cai Lingcai dribbled past three opponents, passing the ball to left-winger Wang Nanzhen. Aigedun arrived quickly, and Wang immediately crossed the ball. Yahui unleashed a powerful shot, and the ball grazed the crossbar before rocketing into the net, leveling the score.

Xu Heng Carelessly Concedes a Goal: After the equalizer, Huosais' momentum surged again. Aqiao dribbled the ball close to the baseline. Ye Lunyan was forced to concede a corner kick. Aqiao took the kick, sending the ball into the penalty area. Xu Heng jumped out of the crowd and caught the ball to clear the danger. Yahui led the team on a counterattack, and a header went slightly wide, startling Hebaite. Unexpectedly, after narrowly escaping disaster, the Huo team's forwards reignited their ambition, launching a five-pronged attack. Heitan Didi's initial assault was thwarted, and Gu Shangxiang desperately resisted. Kangmuden seized an opportunity to shoot. The ball's trajectory wasn't fast, and although Gu Shangxiang managed to touch the ball, Xu Heng carelessly fumbled it, falling awkwardly as the ball slowly rolled into the goal from the left corner, eliciting gasps from the crowd.

Twenty Minutes Wasted: After the start of the afternoon session, Huosais temporarily adopted a defensive posture to conserve energy. Jinan's cavalry charged relentlessly but failed to break through the three lines of defense. Aigedun and Tao Lewei, like a tiger and a leopard, pounced on anyone who came near. Hebaite also displayed great skill. Xu Yahui launched several attacks but was intercepted by Simisi halfway. Qiongsi also tried to find openings, even shouting in the southern territory, but was driven out of bounds by Xiaoyun. Xuebaite made a comeback, and Xiaoyun returned the favor, repeatedly and bravely defending the king, earning the admiration of the fans.

Three Goals Lost in an Instant: Disaster often strikes when least expected. At this moment, Jinan was fully focused on scoring a goal to equalize, but the Huo team's ferocious nature suddenly revealed itself. Qiongsi, aided by Mao Lin, unleashed a powerful shot from twenty yards out, sending the ball diagonally into the net. Soon after, Mao Lin launched another attack, making the score 4-1. Aqiao, still not satisfied, made it 5-1, gaining an absolute advantage. Looking back at Jinan's players, their spirits were scattered, and they were unable to launch a counterattack. Soon, dusk fell, the whistle blew, and the two teams called it a day.

The Expression of Strength 192

— Boyuan

I remember that there was once a term in our literary world: "Literature of Strength."

There was no detailed explanation, but I guess it meant that literary works should not only have a fighting theme, but also have stimulating language. The so-called "sharp," the so-called "active," the so-called "rich in revolutionary emotion" were probably adjectives for the so-called "Literature of Strength."

Literary works have the mission of moving people. However, the power to move people does not lie in the "drawn swords" on the surface of the text. For example, wine, some are very strong on the palate, and some are mellow. Those that are very strong on the palate seem to have a lot of "strength" at the time, but that's all it is later. Those that are mellow on the palate are different: you don't feel its "strength" when you drink it, but when it takes effect later, you really get drunk!

A truly powerful literary work should be a mellow wine. The subject matter is just a simple story, but it contains rich content: it moves people and teaches people imperceptibly. The writing is just fluent and clear, without "amazing strokes" or convoluted structures, but it gives the reader a deep and lasting impression.

The production of such works is conditional, that is, rich life experience and sincere and profound emotions.

But it is not to say that literary works that are very strong on the palate are not desirable. However, writers should not be satisfied with "being strong on the palate."

China is not lacking in aggressive works now, but mellow works that become more and more powerful as you chew on them are still rare. Perhaps this is because Chinese new literature has not yet left the "youth era." The literature of a nation and an era is sometimes similar to that of an individual. Although (the youth era) is dazzling, it must go through a long and arduous creative experience to reach the stage of "maturity."

On Ass-Kissing 193

— Gao Zhi

Mr. Lin Yutang's article on "Kicking Ass" is both broad and refined. "Kicking Ass" is indeed one of China's national quintessence. But in China, ass-kissing is also one of the national quintessence. The meaning of its being a national quintessence is, like national medicine, national studies, etc., not something that all ordinary people can use.

These ass-kissers are also the ones who are "willing" to have their asses kicked.

Why kiss ass? In my opinion, it's probably like this:

There is a saying in the vernacular that says "ascend to heaven in one step." There are people who ascend to heaven, and I won't mention the methods they use to ascend to heaven here. But it is a fact that not everyone can ascend to heaven in one step.

But there are many people who hope to ascend to heaven in one step. They even know that they can't ascend to heaven but hope to be able to rise a little higher, suspended in the air, stepping on people's heads.

Since there are so many people who want to ascend to heaven but can't, they naturally have to think of special methods.

This special method is to find people who can ascend to heaven, hug their asses or thighs, and stick their faces to the waist or ass of the person being hugged. On the one hand, the heat on the face of the ass-kisser can increase the energy of the person ascending to heaven, and on the other hand, the feet of the person ascending to heaven can freely kick the ass of the ass-kisser. In this way, those who want to ascend to heaven but can't also ascend to the sky with others. After they ascend to heaven, whether they fart or pee in the sky, the spectators below watch them playing, happy, and farting on top like watching a kite ascend to heaven. When they are happy, they take out ingots of candy from their pockets, eat them freely, and spit out some residue.

To find an ancient method, it is the favorite minister hugging the king's ass, the minister hugging the ass of the favorite eunuch, the governor hugging the ass of the minister, the county magistrate hugging the ass of the governor, the bailiff hugging the ass of the county magistrate, and even the maids and servants hugging the ass of the bailiff. But between equal relatives, it is okay to hug the waist.

The person ascending to heaven is ass-kissed, and the kisser is also ass-kissed. Therefore, the result is that those who can ascend to heaven cannot ascend very high, and the feet of the ass-kissers often kick the faces of the people below in the air. As for the asses being kissed, there is also a distinction between domestic and foreign goods.

The Ferryman 194

— He Jiahua

If the wind keeps blowing, that's fine; what's scary is a gust of wind, a pause, and then another gust of wind, as if suffering from malaria, even if you're not cold, you'll tremble.

The river water is deep and blue, and when the wind blows, white waves rise everywhere. From the surface of the white waves, cold light shoots out like arrows. The river is very desolate. Those huge sailing ships are all silent, and very few rafts carrying firewood and foreign oil pass by; so this ferry boat crossing the middle of the stream alone is really very lonely.

The ferryman is an old man, wearing an old military uniform, barefoot, but very stubbornly wearing leggings. He is bald, and snot hangs on his sparse beard. If it flows into his mouth, he is busy licking it. Looking at his thin face and listening to his hoarse voice, who would believe that he can row a boat?

"Ferryman, quickly row the boat over here!"

He was originally squatting on the bow of the boat, or hiding in the cabin to steal a sniff of dry tobacco, but when he heard this shout, he had to throw the remaining half of the cigarette away and quickly pick up the bamboo pole, following the water, and row the boat to the other side. It's so cold, if he delays for a moment, then the passengers waiting anxiously on the beach on the other side, waiting in the north wind, will definitely curse him like a dead corpse:

"Are you dead? You still haven't come over after all this time!"

The wind is really fierce, and every time it blows, he has to shrink his whole body and shiver non-stop. Sometimes the ferry boat rocks, as if it will drift away with the current, and the more he rows, the farther he gets from the shore. The bamboo pole that he usually uses so skillfully also seems to have suddenly become unfamiliar, and his frozen hands can't hold it steady, and he almost drops it into the water several times.

Seeing his pitiful appearance, many people muttered: "He's really a dead thing, look at him, how can he row a boat, I think he should just stay at home and eat old rice."

Some said:

"I don't know if he is rowing the boat, or the boat is rowing him!"

But in the midst of all the accusations, the boat was finally rowed to the shore by him. Because the small pier is broken, and the gangplank can't be set up, people wearing shoes and socks can't simply step into the shallow, muddy water: to walk from the beach to the ferry boat, there is no other way but to carry them on your back, and this hard labor is naturally his job again.

"The water is really cold, it's like ice, piercing to the bone, we poor people..."

He bent his back, gasped for breath, and shyly said this from time to time, and looked back at the person on his back, hoping to get some money for wine, but no one paid attention to him, and no one was willing to give him a penny.

Seeing that there was no one else on the shore, he struggled to pick up the bamboo pole again, facing the wind, under the dark and gloomy sky, inch by inch, and rowed the boat back.

"It's really cold today, it's probably going to snow, right?"

Someone suddenly asked halfway.

"My fingers feel like they're falling off."

Someone immediately sighed and answered with a cold breath.

"Old man, the water must be especially cold, aren't you cold rowing the boat all day?"

The ferryman just shook his head and didn't answer, this question is really boring. He frowned and looked at the distant mountains, looking at the wilderness, while shaking the ferry boat, his whole body trembling, and no one understood what he was thinking.

In his constant ferrying back and forth, the day quietly passed, and soon it was dusk.

Although he was lonely during the day, he still heard a little human voice from a few passengers. But at night, on this lonely and desolate river, only he alone slept in the cabin.

"Ferryman, quickly row the boat over here!"

In his dreams, this restless old man would also be awakened by this shout, thinking that someone picking up New Year's goods or walking at night was waiting for him on the other side; but when he poked his head out, he only saw a cold, abyss of night.

Sai Zhenzhu's "New Road" 195

— Shengfu

To this day, I have rarely read Sai Zhenzhu's works. Her "The Good Earth" is said to be a novel depicting the lives of farmers, and it is very successful. However, what I am talking about now is one of her short stories, "The New Road."

Because the author is a famous person, and it is said that "she has long been recognized abroad," I don't want to talk about the words in the field of literary academic. In this point, the article is indeed very successful in this regard.

Now let's talk about the consciousness of "The New Road."

"The New Road" clearly implies two eras. One is that the era when people went to the tiger stove to buy water has passed, and what follows is the era of replacing it with "running hot water pipes." The era of those "small carts, rickshaws, and donkeys crowding around, the narrow and winding small streets built for more than a thousand years has passed, and now it is the era of building a "vast and distant" new road, "not even if all the people in the world come here, it will not be crowded."" "Now is the age of revolution."

"Now is the age of rebellious sons, the age of lazy people," he draws the same two generations of characters in Turgenev's Fathers and Sons.

The father's era is finally over. Although Lu Shun stubbornly sits on the ruins of the tiger stove, watching people tear down the tiles on the roof, "letting the midday sun scorch him," in the end, he can't resist his son's repeated requests and has to "stand up, as if he is very old, hold his son's hand, and follow him."

What is the era that follows? It is that some small carts, donkey carts, and tiger stoves are gone, and on the new road, there are naturally trams, cars, and high-rise foreign buildings, and the owners of foreign buildings. At the same time, outside Beimenkou, on the open space in the nearby fields, there are small grass sheds, not as good as the grass sheds of tiger stoves, and the people who go to the grass sheds.

Although the old man is obsessed with the past, the son is satisfied with the present. Because he can get fifty yuan a month from "this new road," he proudly answers his father: "The new government allows me to." He is very satisfied with being a supervisor. Naturally, he cannot realize that everyone does not want to live in grass sheds and wants to enjoy high-rise buildings equipped with "running hot water." The construction of the new road should no longer have "a cry of crying," and there is no need for such a majestic officer and "three soldiers."

In short: the consciousness of this work is not enough. The era implied by the author has passed in Europe one or two hundred years ago. Although it has begun in China more than thirty years ago and has not yet completed its process, this new road can no longer continue to be opened up according to the old trajectory. It must take a leap and reach another future. Naturally, the author cannot realize this profound point, which is determined by the author's social stratum, and is not surprising. The good weaknesses are thus revealed, and she cannot grasp the practice of China's current stage.

"Where does this new road lead to?" Following the direction implied by the author, we only hear "We are doomed, we are doomed," a cry of crying.

Two Brothers (45) 196

— By Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

He pondered, but could not recall anything. But he must not have looked closely enough, not observed accurately enough, because at the time he had no reason to discover these telltale signs.

He stood up, preparing to return to his own room. He slowly ascended the stairs, still thinking. When passing his brother's door, he suddenly stopped and reached out to open it. He suddenly had a strong desire to see Zhe'an immediately, to look at him for a long time, to see him unexpectedly while he was asleep, when his weariness had subsided, when the lines on his face were relaxed and resting, when all the ugliness of life had disappeared. In this way, he could grasp the secret of his face in sleep; if there were any noteworthy similarities, they would certainly not escape his eyes.

But if Zhe'an woke up, what would he say? How would he explain his reason for going to see him?

He stood still, his fingers tightly gripping the doorknob, pondering a reason, an excuse.

He suddenly remembered that eight days ago, he had lent his brother a bottle of opium tincture for toothache (Laudanum). He could say that he himself had a toothache tonight and was going to retrieve his medicine. So he went in, walking stealthily like a pickpocket.

Zhe'an slept soundly with his lips slightly parted, like an animal. His golden beard and hair stained the white sheet with a golden blot. He did not wake up at all, but he stopped snoring.

Bier bent down, looking at him greedily. No, this young man in front of him did not resemble Roland; then he remembered again the lost small portrait of Maraisa. He had to find this portrait! Looking at that portrait, he might not doubt anymore.

His brother moved, certainly because he was standing in front of him, or because the light of the candle shone into his eyes and disturbed his sleep. So the doctor retreated, tiptoed to the door, and quietly closed it. Then he returned to his own room, but he did not go to sleep.

Dawn broke very slowly. The clock in the dining room ticked away, its sound deep and solemn, as if a large cathedral bell were hidden inside this small piece of clockwork. The sound traveled up the empty staircase, through the walls and doors, disappearing into the dull ears of the sleeping people in the room. Bier paced back and forth between his bed and the window. What should he do? He felt too agitated to spend the day in his family. He hoped to be isolated from everyone for at least one day, so that he could reflect, calm down, and gather his spirits to face the necessary return to daily life.

Okay! He could go to Trouville to see the crowds frolicking on the beach. This could dispel his sorrow, change his thoughts, and give him time to prepare for the terrible things he had discovered.

As soon as it was light, he washed and dressed. The fog had cleared, and the weather was very good. Because the boat to Trouville would not leave the pier until nine o'clock, the doctor thought he should kiss his mother before leaving.

He waited until her usual time to get up and went downstairs. When he reached her door, his heart was beating so hard that he had to stop and breathe. His hand resting on the lock was weak and trembling, and he barely had the strength to turn the doorknob and go into the room. He knocked on the door. His mother's voice asked:

"Who is it?"

"Me, Bier."

"What's the matter?"

"Because I'm going to Trouville with some friends to play for a day, I came to say goodbye to you first."

"But I haven't gotten up yet."

"Okay, then don't get up. I'll kiss you when I come back tonight."
