Telegraphs Created by the Voice of the Electric Realm and the Times 197

— Lü Bing

The times are enough to create heroes, and heroes are also enough to create the times; but based on the experience of the telecommunications industry, the two words "times" can indeed produce multiple views of telegrams. Therefore, it is not impossible to say that telegraphs are created by the times.

When the situation is peaceful and society is tranquil, the communications of officials and the military are relatively reduced. But when political affairs suddenly change and the situation suddenly becomes tense, those who want to communicate do so, those who want to denounce do so, those who want to inquire do so, and those who want to report do so. The telegram business increases accordingly; the telegraph lines become crowded accordingly. This kind of phenomenon can truly be said to be created by the times.

Telecommunications personnel serve the country and society. Busy telegrams are their duty, and they have no choice but to do their duty. But looking at the current situation, the whole country, from top to bottom, is trying to unite with utmost sincerity, but the changes of the times are unexpected. When we see telegrams flying around and hear the whirring of the telegraph machines, this work is non-stop all night. On the one hand, we are working hard to defend our position, and at the same time, we seem to hear the call for peace.

Comparison of New and Old International Telegraph Regulations on Plain and Cipher Language Provisions Wang Yunzhen 198

Telegrams are the key to international communication and also a tool for cultural exchange. The business can only thrive if people all over the world can make full use of telegrams. But in order to achieve this goal, there must be two prerequisites: (1) That the telegraph language is not subject to any restrictions, and all countries participating in the International Telegraph Convention can use their respective national languages to send telegrams; (2) That the combination of telegram texts should be simplified and standardized, so as to calculate the number of words and facilitate transmission. Over the years, telegraph experts from various countries have paid attention to this. At each International Telegraph Conference, there have been additions and revisions to the business rules and regulations. This is because world telecommunications traffic is becoming increasingly complex, and the business rules must be revised from time to time to be applicable.

The current International Telegraph Business Regulations are those revised in Paris in 1925 and Beijing in 1928. Last year (1932), the International Telegraph Conference was held in Madrid, and there were many revisions to these regulations. The Ministry of Communications has translated the original book into Chinese and will soon publish it. The main differences between the new and old regulations regarding plain and cipher language telegrams are explained below:

(1) In the old regulations, the languages allowed to be used were limited to German, English, Spanish, French, Dutch, Italian, Portuguese, Latin, and Esperanto. (Chinese characters composed of four numbers are also allowed to be used.)

In the new regulations, in addition to the nine languages listed on the right, there are also Abyssinian, African, etc., totaling fifty-six languages. (Chinese characters are still allowed to be used.)

(2) In the old regulations, plain language can use letters such as AAA NOU, as well as punctuation marks (;), exclamation marks, and marks before and after the predicate (;).

(3) The old regulations allowed the use of cross ciphers, but there were certain restrictions on the spelling of letters. Counting words was very difficult, and because there were too many cross combinations, errors were easily made during transmission.

The new regulations abolish cross ciphers and only allow the use of five-letter ciphers, which are not subject to any restrictions. Counting words is easy, and errors can be reduced during transmission.

(4) In the old regulations, five-letter cipher telegrams started with four words, and the fee was charged at two-thirds of the full price. In the new regulations, five-letter cipher telegrams start with five words, and the fee is charged at six-tenths of the full price.

(5) In the old regulations, number words (not those expressed in letters) contained in five-letter cipher telegrams could not be mixed, except for those indicating trademarks or commercial marks.

The new regulations allow the use of number words or groups of number words in cipher telegrams, but they must not exceed half of the total number of words charged in the telegram.

According to the provisions of the new regulations, plain language telegrams are open to as many as fifty-six national languages, and cipher language telegrams only use five-letter ciphers. The former seeks to universalize telegraph language, while the latter seeks to simplify telegraph cipher language, both of which are major improvements compared to the old regulations. People all over the world should be happy to use them. Our country is one of the member states of the International Telegraph Convention, and the revised articles in the new regulations will be implemented from January 1st of next year (the 23rd year of the Republic of China). The people of the country should pay attention to this. It is heard that the International Telecommunications Bureau has already sent an official letter to notify them.

Improvements in Telegraph Business in the Past Year (Middle) 199

— Liu Junxiang

(4) Using local telephone to send and receive telegrams According to this method, all telephone users can apply to the local telegraph office to have telegrams sent from other places transmitted by telephone, or to have telegrams sent to other places transmitted by telephone to the office for dispatch. They only need to pay a registration fee of one yuan to be valid for one year. After the telegram has been transmitted by telephone, the bottom of the telegram will still be sent to the other party on the same day for verification. This method can greatly speed up the transmission of telegrams.

(5) Replacing the addressee's address with a telephone number. Checking the addressee's address is not related to the content of the telegram, but it often contains lengthy words, which is not economical to charge by the word. The Ministry of Communications has established a method to replace the addressee's address with a telephone number. All addressees with a telephone can use the telephone number to replace their address, adding a "phone" character before the number to identify it. No matter how many numbers there are, they are all charged as one word. This is very economical for the sender. The above-mentioned fourth method is also a combination of telegram and telephone.

(6) Revising the special delivery fee method. Checking the telegram sending and receiving method originally stipulated that if the addressee's address is more than five li away from the office, a special delivery fee will be charged. However, now the roads in various cities have been improved. If it exceeds five li, a special delivery fee will be charged, which is difficult to satisfy the sender, and the messenger often uses it as an excuse to demand more money, which has an impact on the reputation of the office. The Ministry of Communications has revised the method, stipulating that if the addressee's address and the office are in the same city, no special delivery fee will be charged regardless of the distance. If they are not in the same city and the distance exceeds five li, a special delivery fee may be charged. This revision is a loss for the office and a saving for the addressee.

(7) Chinese telegrams can use Arabic numerals. Chinese telegrams must be translated into telegraph codes for transmission due to technical reasons. Therefore, the house number in the address and the amount of money and the quantity of goods in the telegram must be written in characters, and cannot be expressed in Arabic numerals, in order to avoid code confusion. This provision requires a lot of words. The Ministry of Communications has now approved the method of referring to foreign language telegrams, and the above-mentioned house numbers and various numbers can be written in Arabic numerals, and parentheses are placed before and after them for identification. The fee calculation method is that one to four Arabic numerals are counted as one word for plain language, and one to five Arabic numerals are counted as one word for cipher language. Parentheses are free of charge and can be used with decimal points to calculate one Arabic numeral. This method can save money for sending telegrams with numbers: for example, "No. 1123 Zhongshan Road" can be written as "No. (1123) Zhongshan Road", which can save six words; and "4399 yuan, 1 jiao, 6 fen, 5 li" can be written as "4399.165", which can save as many as eleven words.

Significance of Recovering the Telegraph Sending and Receiving Rights of Submarine Cable Companies (Continued) 200

— He Shui

(B) Preventing unfavorable propaganda by foreigners.

Before the recovery of the sending and receiving rights, all incoming and outgoing telegrams were received and delivered by the Sanshui Cable Company itself, and we had no say in the matter. Therefore, foreigners in China could freely report unfavorable news to various countries, and we had no way to stop them. As a result, people in various countries were deceived by this propaganda and did not understand the true situation of our country, which led to various negative impressions of us. Now that the right to send and receive telegrams has been taken into our own hands, all telegrams must pass through our hands, which can be strictly checked. The above-mentioned unfavorable events in our country can no longer occur.

(C) Understanding the handling of submarine cable telegrams.

Since the sending and receiving of submarine cable telegrams was handled by various companies in the past, their situation was unknown. Now that all incoming and outgoing telegrams are handled by us, the business situation can be understood. Moreover, in the past, in order to develop their business and attract telegram business, various companies often handled telegram business in a way that did not comply with the International Telegraph Business Regulations. Now that the sending and receiving of telegrams is handled by us, it can be gradually corrected to ensure that the regulations are in compliance. The important significance of recovering the telegraph sending and receiving rights of the Sanshui Cable Company has been described above. What kind of understanding should people from all walks of life in Shanghai have about this matter? The main points are as follows:

(A) Should recognize the proper name of the three sending and receiving offices.

Since May 1st of this year, the organization in Shanghai that receives telegrams sent to various foreign countries via the three cable companies has been the "Telegraph Office for Cablegram via Eastern Extension Cables, Great Northern Cables, Commercial Pacific Cable, Bureau of International Telegraphs, Ministry of Communications," and not the former Eastern Extension, Great Northern, and Commercial Pacific Cable Companies. The messengers who deliver telegrams sent from various foreign countries are also the messengers of the above-mentioned three sending and receiving offices, and not the messengers of the former three companies. Since the affiliation has changed and the name has been changed, people from all walks of life in Shanghai should deeply recognize the name of "Telegraph Office for Cablegram via Eastern Extension Cables, Great Northern Cables, Commercial Pacific Cable, Bureau of International Telegraphs, Ministry of Communications" in order to respect our national sovereignty and express patriotic thoughts, and should no longer deeply imprint the names of the former Eastern Extension, Great Northern, and Commercial Pacific Companies in their minds.

(B) Should recognize the organizational nature of the three sending and receiving offices.

All the staff and messengers of the three sending and receiving offices are appointed and employed by the Ministry of Communications and have nothing to do with the former three cable companies. Therefore, people from all walks of life in Shanghai should clearly understand that the three sending and receiving offices are agencies under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Communications, and their status is exactly the same as the International Radio Station in the Sassoon Building on Beijing Road, the Telegraph Bureau of the Ministry of Communications on Sichuan Road, and the Wireless Radio Station on Minguo Road, and they are not agencies run by foreigners.

(C) Should recognize the current procedures for handling telegram business.

At present, the Eastern Extension, Great Northern, and Commercial Pacific Cable Companies have no right to handle telegram business externally. All matters related to the receipt, delivery, and inquiry of submarine cable telegrams should be handled directly by the three sending and receiving offices. In the future, if people from all walks of life have any matters related to incoming and outgoing submarine cable telegrams, they should call or write to the three sending and receiving offices to contact them, and should no longer use the names of the Eastern Extension, Great Northern, and Commercial Pacific Companies, so as to avoid various misunderstandings and delay important matters. In the past few months, the outside world has not been very clear about this situation, and many people still mistakenly use the names of the companies to contact the three sending and receiving offices, which hinders the handling of affairs and is unfavorable to the people themselves. It is hoped that people from all walks of life in Shanghai will pay close attention to this point to correct the above-mentioned errors.

At present, various industries in our country are striving for reform and progress. The rights that were previously seized by foreigners are also gradually being recovered. The cancellation of the direct sending and receiving of telegrams by the various cable companies and the formation of the three submarine cable telegraph sending and receiving offices are also proceeding along these lines. It is hoped that people from all walks of life in Shanghai will deeply recognize the current status and situation of the three sending and receiving offices and jointly maintain the integrity of our country's telecommunications sovereignty. This is not only the good fortune of the telecommunications administration, but also the glory of the country. As for the staff of the three sending and receiving offices, they should work hard according to the regulations. At the very least, they must maintain the efficiency of the company era in the past, and further strive for various improvements, so as to fulfill their duty to serve the public and live up to the earnest expectations of all parties.

(Note) The Chinese and Western names of the three submarine cable telegraph sending and receiving offices

Telegraph Office for Cablegram via Eastern Extension Cables, Bureau of International Telegraphs, Ministry of Communications

Telegraph Office for Cablegram via Great Northern Cables, Bureau of International Telegraphs, Ministry of Communications

Telegraph Office for Cablegram via Commercial Pacific Cable, Bureau of International Telegraphs, Ministry of Communications (End)

Welcome Marconi, the Inventor of Wireless Radio A Telecommunications Reporter 201

The fame of Guglielmo Marconi, the inventor of wireless radio, is as widespread as the dissemination of wireless radio around the world, and is almost known to every woman and child. The Century of Progress International Exposition held in Chicago, USA this year officially designated October 2 as Marconi Day. On this day, Marconi performed at the meeting and sent the S signal, which was transmitted around the world and returned to its original location in about one minute. This S signal is the symbol that Marconi used to communicate across the Atlantic with Newfoundland in the United Kingdom in late 1901.

Many people from all walks of life know about Marconi's history, and it has also been published in recent maritime newspapers, so there is no need to repeat it. In short, Marconi studied and invented in the laboratory as a student, making wireless radio a powerful tool for communication, benefiting both military and civilian use. His contribution to human welfare is second to none among modern inventors.

Now Marconi has actually traveled across the ocean to visit China. Although our country's wireless business is still in its infancy, it has been planned and operated by the transportation authorities and our country's experts. International long-distance communication has now taken shape. With the guidance of advanced experts, the development of the business is even more promising. When people in our telecommunications industry hear this news, they sincerely welcome Marconi, the inventor of wireless radio.

Telecommunications Talks Telephone丨Automatic Watch丨Dialing the Number Plate丨First Serve as a Driver 202

The telephone is called "automatic," but the machine itself is not actually automatic. Everything still has to be commanded by people to initiate action. Therefore, the word "automatic" means that the user operates the connection himself, so it is different from the ordinary use of a telephone that requires a driver.

Working together

The telephone does not require a driver, so the driver's duties are transferred to the user himself. When the earpiece is in hand, the fingertip is inserted into the number plate and rotated, going back and forth, turning smoothly. During this short period of time, the user is not a user, but actually a telephone driver. When the conversation can be heard and the language has reached, the earpiece is gently placed down and the person is also away. At this moment, the user is not a user, but also a telephone driver (because after the phone is placed on the hook, the related components inside the telephone exchange immediately return to normal, as if the driver has disconnected the line).

Since the user also serves as a driver, how does he drive? How does he connect? This is what the reader wants to know (this is for general users who know how to use the machine but do not know the mechanical situation). First, a brief explanation of the number plate on the phone is given.

When using the telephone for the first time, pick up the earpiece. At this time, the user's line has been connected to the telephone exchange, and a buzzing sound can be heard. The buzzing sound is called "dial tone" in telephone terminology. Since it is "dial tone," you can dial the number with confidence. So dial the number plate with confidence (if there is no buzzing sound, it means that there is no "dial tone," which means that the line is blocked or there is no free line).

The appearance of the plate and its contents are shown in the attached picture. Those who are used to it will recognize it at a glance. The main part inside the plate is a spring that can extend and release. Due to its rotational force, it causes the electrical key that is connected to it to open and close the current. This current is like the pulse of a human body. The number of times is the same as the number dialed, and the speed is controlled by the internal rotary wheel. Each time the number plate is rotated to the limit, the finger is released, and the plate also rotates back. At this time, the pulse current continues to fluctuate, flowing into the telephone exchange equipment, and the mechanical action completes the connection procedure between the two parties. In this way, is the user not a driver? The user is indeed a driver.

It is quite beneficial to consider that the user also serves as a driver in social use. First, by connecting the lines yourself, as long as the number is dialed correctly, the user being called is not on the phone, and there is no one who cannot be connected correctly. Second, in places where people from all walks of life gather and speak different languages, the driver often mishears the reported number, resulting in incorrect connections, or the user being called is busy, and the user mistakenly believes that the driver is intentionally delaying the connection. All of these can be directly understood without the need for explanation (the mechanical benefits are not discussed here). This is why the users of the Capital Telephone Bureau have found it extremely convenient since the installation of automatic telephones, and the telephones run by the Ministry of Communications, such as those in Shanghai and Wuhan, have also been renovated to install automatic telephones (the mechanical situation inside the bureau will be discussed in the next issue).

Advertisement Telegrams in Germany 203

A few years ago, Germany added the distribution of telegrams (TM) to its domestic telegram business. Because the fees were still cheap, the business community used it as a promotional tool for sales. Later, they felt that there was a need for a special telegram to facilitate advertising. The fees for this telegram should be low, and the delivery location should not be limited to one corner.

The German telecommunications authorities are well aware of the urgency of this need and have now created what is called an advertisement telegram in their domestic business. Its nature is a slow telegram, and the number of copies is stipulated to be at least one thousand. The number of words in each telegram must not exceed one hundred, and the delivery address can be the same or different.

The bottom of this telegram should be marked with the delivery address and delivered to the sending and receiving office two days (working days) before the expected delivery date. At the same time, the sender should make a copy for each addressee, and the telegraph bureau will provide the required copy paper free of charge. The telegraph bureau will then deliver these copies as letter telegrams.

The fees to be charged for advertisement telegrams:

(A) Five pfennigs per word for the bottom of the telegram

(B) Ten pfennigs for each copy, regardless of the number of words

(C) If the addressee's address is not in the same location as the sending office, an additional one pfennig per copy will be charged

(However, at least five pfennigs should be paid for each different location)

For example, the number of words for which the bottom of an advertisement telegram should be charged is:

3 (address) + 50 (text) + 3 (signature) ▲ 56

Telegraph Inquiry Guidelines 204

Z> Qinghua

(I) Guidelines for Recipients Inquiring About Telegrams

3. If a telegram has not been delivered to the recipient, and the sender notifies them that a telegram was sent on a certain day, but the telegraph office has not delivered it, the recipient should first inquire with the telegraph office to see if a telegram arrived on that day. If the office has not received it, then the telegram must have been missed by an intermediate office or not sent by the originating office. The recipient should notify the sender to take the original telegraph receipt to the originating office for inquiry. If the inquiry confirms that the telegram was missed, not forwarded, or not delivered due to an error by the telegraph office, the sender can request a full refund of the telegraph fee from the originating office.

4. Telegram Delay: If the recipient receives a telegram and discovers that it arrived late (the date and time noted at the top of the telegram form indicate when the sender submitted the telegram, which can be compared with the time of receipt to determine if there was a delay. The permissible delay time for domestic telegrams is generally the same as postal delivery, unless otherwise specified for international telegrams). The recipient can take the telegram to the telegraph office to inquire about the cause of the delay. If the delay was due to line problems, congestion, or being held up by military censors, the telegraph fee cannot be refunded. However, if the delay was due to negligence on the part of the telegraph office, the recipient can send the telegram to the sender to request a refund of the telegraph fee from the originating office.

5. Inquiring About the Sender's Name: Sometimes, the recipient receives a telegram without the sender's signature, making it impossible to know who sent it. The recipient can take the telegram to the telegraph office and request a paid public telegram to inquire about the sender's name. In addition to the six-character fee for the telegram itself, a prepaid reply fee of four or five characters is also required. For clarity in calculating the fees, examples of paid public telegrams are provided below:

(I) The outgoing paid public telegram is calculated as six characters:

=RCX= 645 Sixteenth Smith SenderssNamc

Paid identification, i.e., telegram number, telegram date, telegram recipient's name, please inquire about the sender's name, prepaid reply fee.

(II) The incoming paid public telegram is calculated as four characters:

I26 Seventeenth Srrith John

Outgoing telegram number, outgoing telegram date, original telegram recipient's name, original telegram sender's name.

6. Inquiring About Errors in the Name of the Originating Office: The foreign place name written in the "Originating Office Name" field at the top of the telegram form indicates where the telegram was sent from. Sometimes this place name may be transmitted incorrectly by the telegraph office, such as "Cangzhou" being mistaken for "Cangkou." In such cases, the recipient, upon receiving the telegram, may suspect that the sender has moved to a certain place. For the sake of caution, the recipient can take the telegram to the telegraph office and use a paid public telegram to inquire about the name of the originating office. If the inquiry confirms that the error was made by the telegraph office, the prepaid fee for the outgoing and incoming paid public telegrams can be fully refunded. If there is no error, the fee cannot be refunded. 7. Requesting Telegrams to be Forwarded Elsewhere: Sometimes, the recipient anticipates a telegram to be sent to them at a certain location, but due to urgent matters, they need to travel elsewhere. To avoid the telegram being undeliverable or delayed, they can submit a letter to the telegraph office requesting that their telegrams be forwarded to the location they will be traveling to. However, they must prove that they are the intended recipient (to prevent others from fraudulently receiving telegrams) and be responsible for the forwarding fee.

7. Incorrect Telegram Delivery: Sometimes, telegrams are delivered incorrectly due to unclear addresses, similar business names, or negligence on the part of the telegraph office messenger. If the recipient discovers that the telegram is not intended for them, they should immediately return it to the telegraph office or notify the telegraph office by phone to have a messenger collect it for immediate redelivery. Do not forward it yourself to avoid misunderstandings.

8. Incorrect Telegram Date: If the recipient receives a telegram and suspects that the original telegram's sent date may be incorrect, or if the telegram's content is related to the original telegram's date (e.g., "Departing tomorrow"), they can take the telegram to the telegraph office and send a paid public telegram to inquire. If the inquiry confirms that the error was made by the telegraph office, the fee for the paid public telegram can be fully refunded.

9. Omissions in Telegram Translation: According to regulations, the telegraph office should translate the telegram's code into text. If there are omissions in the translation or requests for translation fees, the recipient can send the telegram to the Telegraph Administration Department of the Ministry of Transportation in Nanjing to request an investigation and have the responsible personnel at the telegraph office punished.

10. Procedures for Sending Prepaid Reply Telegrams: If the characters "RPX" (indicating a prepaid reply fee) appear before the recipient's place name or name in the telegram, the receiving office will attach a prepaid reply fee voucher when delivering the telegram. The recipient can use this voucher to send a reply telegram. If the fee for the reply telegram exceeds the prepaid amount, the sender of the reply telegram must pay the difference. If the fee is less than the prepaid amount, the recipient can ask the telegraph office for a note stating the remaining unused amount, which the recipient can send to the sender to request a refund from the originating office (unused amounts below 40 cents for domestic telegrams or 2 gold francs for international telegrams cannot be refunded).

If three hundred copies are sent locally, and seven hundred copies are sent to other locations, the total cost will be 309.66 marks, averaging approximately 0.26 marks per copy (equivalent to about 30 cents in Chinese currency).

Merchants who spend this small amount and gain the assistance of telegraphic power can certainly achieve their advertising goals.

Ordinary printed advertisements can be recognized at a glance, and recipients often throw them into the wastebasket. However, using the above method, every recipient who receives a telegram will undoubtedly open and read it.

News from the Semi-Monthly News Agency 205

New International Telegraph Regulations to Take Effect on New Year's Day: The International Telegraph Regulations were amended at the International Telegraph Conference in Kyoto, Madrid last year. Among them, the regulations on telegraph fees, such as express telegrams being charged twice the rate of ordinary telegrams, have been implemented since April 1 of this year. Other changes regarding the method for coded telegrams will be implemented from New Year's Day next year. These measures are extremely important. The following is a summary for merchants' reference.

1. The old "Class A" code words (i.e., code words consisting of ten letters) are abolished.

2. Each code word is limited to five letters. The method of composition is unrestricted except that accented letters are not allowed. The presence or absence of vowel letters in each word is optional.

3. Coded telegrams are charged at 60% of the full rate telegram fee (domestic telegrams are still charged at the full rate). Each telegram is calculated with a minimum of five words.

4. The recipient's name, address, and the sender's signature within the coded telegram are still calculated as one word for every fifteen letters.

The First Draft of the National Language Telegraph Compilation is Completed and Under Review: The Ministry of Transportation, in order to promote the use of the National Language in telegrams, specially appointed Chen Yiyu and Qiu Wenbing to compile a National Language Telegraph Compilation. After several months, the first draft has now been completed. However, for the sake of prudence, the Ministry recently sent Chen Yiyu to Beiping with the first draft to be reviewed by the National Language Unification Preparatory Committee in order to perfect it. Once the review is completed, it will be ready for implementation.

Temporary Telegraph Stations Established in Disaster Areas: Recently, in order to facilitate communication in the Yellow River flood disaster area and to facilitate relief work, the Ministry of Transportation has established telegraph stations in Kaifeng, Lanfeng, Changyuan, Xiaopangzhuang, and other places, and has dispatched many telegraph operators to work in these locations.

Capital Pilot Program for Receiving Telegrams via Telephone: In large metropolitan areas with vast territories, although telegraph offices and radio stations have several branches and receiving/sending points, the public still finds it laborious to send telegrams. Recently, the Ministry of Transportation, in imitation of the method used by commercial telegraph companies in the United States, has formulated a method for notifying recipients by telephone. It has ordered the Nanjing Telegraph Office and Radio Station to pilot this program first. If the pilot program is successful and there are no obstacles, it will gradually be promoted in major cities such as Shanghai, Tianjin, Hankou, and Beiping to benefit the public. The content of this method is that whenever the public sends a telegram, they can notify the telegraph office or radio station by telephone to send personnel to their residence to collect the telegram and fee, so that the telegram can be sent without leaving their home, and no additional service fee will be charged.

Spring and Autumn

Skimping on Work and Materials 206

— Wei Jing

Relying on the mountain when living by the mountain, relying on the sea when living by the sea, so every trade, ancient and modern, high and low, knows the trick of "skimping on work and materials," and euphemistically calls it, "Every trade produces an expert."

Now, let's take a clear and common example. Suppose you want to make a long gown, naturally you should consult a tailor. Then the tailor will have to play tricks on you. Even if you are very shrewd, and you have 12.5 feet of fabric and want him to make a long gown of 3.9 feet, you think you won't be cheated. But the tailor will relentlessly iron your 11.5 feet into 13 feet, cut off half a foot, and sell it to a scrap shop. If the scorching iron cannot save the day, then at the very least, he will steal 3 or 4 inches to make children's shoe material. As for the stitching, naturally he will use the "paste-lifting principle," even if he can save three or five stitches, it's good, because it saves three or five stitches' worth of time.

However, you can skimp as much as you want. No matter what, you can't skimp so much that the seams split open after only an inch or three stitches when you put it on. You can reduce materials as much as you want, but you can't reduce so much that a 3.9-foot gown is only 3.8 feet, and the customer grabs you by the collar and gives you a big slap in the face. Naturally, there has to be a limit to skimping on work and materials. You have to consider the advantages and disadvantages, and think before you act. Otherwise, you'll not only have your old signboard smashed, but you'll probably never have another customer come to your door. Only by skimping on work and materials just right can you gain both fame and fortune.

Cats can't help but love the smell of fish, and black eyes can't help but light up at the sight of silver. So, no matter what business you're in, making a little extra on the side is excusable in heaven and earth. Because those who are upright and poor are outdated and no longer worth promoting. But then again, you also have to put on a show when you make extra money, to deceive the world. If you only care about the substance and not the appearance, and play a set of "Prime Minister Hefei makes the empire thin," then you're not skilled enough to be considered an expert at "skimping on work and materials."

Nostalgia 207

— Fu Yizhi

The mood of a young man is brave, active, and desperate, pursuing the future, because the magical "hope" is enticing him, beckoning to him, and he can't help but shout forward, go crazy, and try to catch up with it – hope! The old man is already exhausted, "hope" has abandoned him in the boundless desert and fled far away. So he feels lonely and isolated. What else can he do but savor the fragments of his past life's journey, which are relatively meaningful? What else can he ask for? However, I, who am not old and can sometimes mingle in the ranks of the young, am also disheartened, unenterprising, and disgusted with reality, and I begin to savor the past that has long disappeared.

In fact, in the short, ordinary course of my past life, there are indeed some thought-provoking impressions left. The most profound of these impressions, and the one that I feel I can never erase, is the scene from my childhood when I was studying in my hometown of Nanyan.

Nanyan has eight scenic spots. Among the eight scenic spots, "One Drop Spring" and "Five-Level Peak" are the most famous, followed by "Kaijian Pond" and "Zhuoying Well." The remaining four scenic spots were probably named by later generations' fanciful ideas, and newcomers to this place are at a loss. Here is a dome-shaped stone chamber that can hold thousands of people. On the left side of the cave entrance, there is a nipple-like overhanging stone from which clear spring water drips all year round. This is "One Drop Spring." The mountain range gently extends from the side of the cave, then turns towards the front of the cave and rises steeply, dividing into five levels that gradually rise higher. This is what I call "Five-Level Peak." The cave is surrounded by mountains on all sides. You can't see the cave at all unless you're at the foot of Five-Level Peak. Because Zhu Xi and Lu Xiangshan of the Song Dynasty once lectured here, it shares a bit of historical fame with White Deer Cave under the Five Old Men Peak of Mount Lu.

Two majestic and spacious buildings were built inside the cave. The one on the right is a Buddhist hall for Sakyamuni and the like, and the one on the left is the Zhu Wengong Ancestral Hall, which is our school. Because the school's management is lax, studying and playing are as casual as can be. When we don't feel like going to class, we invite our classmates to climb Five-Level Peak or fish in Kaijian Pond. At night, the crystal clear moon shines diagonally on the lush and dense bamboo, penetrating the grass courtyard in front of the cave like duckweed on the surface of a calm lake. We sit, stand, talk, laugh, and perform boxing. Sometimes, we sing at the top of our lungs, and the valleys give us long echoes, and the birds are startled and chirp in response. How can those who are confined in cities full of tension imagine these carefree, happy, and natural lives?

"Hope" for me is like a drowning man seeking light and a way out at the bottom of the water. The more desperately I pursue it, the less light there is, and the more it's a dead end. Only this fragmentary, unadulterated life of the past is worth savoring and counts as a golden page in my life's history. Is it possible to have it again in this life?

New Theft Technique 210

— Gao Yahun

Shanghai is full of strange and wonderful things. As the saying goes, "Turtles, thieves, and robbers, as long as money is involved," so the methods of making money are conceived so miraculously that they are incomprehensible. Recently, Russian girls often come and go in the offices of large foreign-style buildings everywhere. Some hold a paper box or leather suitcase in their hands, containing some items that can be sold. Some pretend to be mentally ill, staring blankly ahead without saying a word. They enter the office after hearing that someone is inside, and leave after taking a look, closing the door behind them. If no one is there, or only the tea boy on duty, they use their clever skills to make objects placed on the desk or in drawers disappear. This is especially true on Saturday afternoons or Sundays, because at this time, the managers and staff of the offices are on holiday and their footsteps are not seen in the offices. The only ones left are a group of junior clerks and servants. These people are rarely in contact with outsiders. Seeing a member of the opposite sex, they are as surprised and happy as Napoleon discovering a new continent. Moreover, when a foreign member of the opposite sex is present, with the senior staff not around to restrain them, who wouldn't want to take advantage of the situation and use their still-unskilled English to strike up a conversation? This is their opportunity. Sometimes, they get so confused that they lose things without even knowing it. This terrifying and amazing theft technique makes one admire your profundity!

Miscellaneous Notes

No Freedom in Diet 212

— Pei Yu

Most of those soaring in the sky piloting airplanes are smokers, and many of them are "old smoking guns," smoking a lot. This is very dangerous. Authorities in the aviation world have instructed us that smoking is the worst thing a pilot can do, because smoking often dries out their throats. When a pilot rapidly descends from a very high altitude, the sudden change in pressure is drastic and difficult to endure. This situation is enough to make his entire head feel strange and start to ring, causing him to become dizzy. The only way to avoid this unpleasant problem is to constantly swallow saliva, because the action of swallowing can open the tubes that run from the back of the throat to the eardrums.

Therefore, the instructors at British flight training schools advise general pilots to constantly chew spearmint gum (commonly known as chewing gum, Western name Chew Gum). Chewing spearmint gum can keep the throat moist and make it easier to swallow saliva. Spearmint gum is not a necessary food, but pilots have to chew it to avoid danger. This reminds me of a fact that people don't pay much attention to.

That fact is that there is no freedom in diet. Everyone knows that people have absolute freedom in diet, but that's not entirely true. Diet is like speech, and in certain special circumstances, it cannot be completely free. For example, the nutrients contained in the food we eat every day must be balanced and complete. Protein, carbohydrates, fats, starches, vitamins, and other elements are indispensable. If one element is missing, it will cause a difficult-to-treat disease. This is scientific proof that diet is not completely free. We can also get some evidence from customs. For example, Shandong people must eat garlic with every meal, Sichuan people must add chili peppers to every dish, Annamites often chew betel nuts, and Mongolians must eat dairy products. Once these commonly eaten foods are forbidden, they will feel uncomfortable all over and even get sick. Furthermore, people who are sick must have all food items approved by a doctor before they can eat them. This means there is absolutely no freedom in diet. The Chinese people pay great attention to the color, aroma, and taste of food, but not so much to the quality, composition, and nutrition. So, except in certain special circumstances, the Chinese people's diet can be said to be very free. The Western people are not like that. In many factories and occupations, certain foods are considered particularly valuable, certain laborers must have a special food, and some are even forced to drink "milk cocoa." Which is more beneficial, absolute freedom in diet or not completely free? That needs to be determined by experts, we dare not say rashly.

That certain foods are particularly valuable for certain occupations is not just empty talk, there is indeed evidence. For example, the food that loggers living in the northwestern part of England rely on for a living is mostly pork and beans. These loggers do very hard work in cold climates, and the energy they expend must be replenished by their food. So they eat pork and beans, because apart from these two things, there is no mixed food that can generate more heat and muscle. Loggers also eat large amounts of bannock, a thick, flat cake simmered in syrup. The syrup has been experimentally shown to contain pure sugar, almost 100% carbohydrates, and carbohydrates are what produce heat. People who work with their brains should often eat white fish. As people used to think, white fish provides phosphorus that nourishes the brain. This view is absurd and unbelievable, but fish is very suitable for people in sedentary occupations and lives, because fish provides a rich and abundant quality of meat, Western name Butchers Meat, which digests quickly and easily. People who work with their brains should take fish as their main food.

Financial Exchange Closing Suddenly Contracts, Gold Price Recovers 1.9 Yuan; U.S. Market Closed on the 30th, Gold Price Fluctuates Slightly, This Month's Notes Settled at 730 Yuan 213

After the gold market declined the previous day, it stabilized slightly yesterday. With the U.S. market closed on the 30th, the market was extremely calm. Talks

The Class of the "Qingke" (Literary Retainers) 233

— Wei Ba

A "qingke" is not a profession in itself, yet in China, there are those who make it their profession; the "muke" (private secretaries) of the past were like this. The cultivation of this custom probably occurred during the feudal era. Generally, declining literati, unable to establish themselves independently as officials or magistrates, and unwilling to languish at home with their wives until old age, would, after tiring of sitting on the sidelines, seek a chance to advance. Thus, they had no choice but to rely on the patronage of powerful families, serving as "qingke." The lives of these individuals depended on catering to their masters' wishes, stirring up trouble, and adding fuel to the flames to sustain their parasitic existence. To outsiders, their situation seemed pitiable, but these individuals were often pleased with themselves and even boasted about it, which reveals their character.

The purpose of being a "qingke" is to amuse others, or in other words, to provide entertainment. Their individuality is lost in the environment, so they cannot act independently in anything, to show that they are independently born people. Instead, they follow the commands of others, seeking to obtain a little leftover for their satisfaction.

However, the term "amuse" is difficult to define. First, one must understand the personality of others; second, one must possess some talent to be slick, skilled and all things to all men. Otherwise, they will inevitably flatter someone but end up putting their foot in it.

I once read Liang Zhangju's "Gui Tian Suo Ji," which contains a section on "qingke," saying, "There are many 'qingke' in the capital, but they must also possess some talent and character to be able to support themselves. Some have compiled a ten-character formula: 'First-rate calligraphy, second-rate talent, three-jin wine capacity, four seasons of clothing, five-man weiqi game, six acts of Kunqu opera, seven-character crooked poems, eight hands of mahjong, ninth-rank official title, and ten parts amiability.'" In just a few dozen words, a vivid portrait of a "qingke" is drawn, which can be called concise and comprehensive. However, Liang's discussion refers to the "qingke" of that time, so it is slightly different from the current situation. If one wants to paint a portrait of a modern "qingke," it should be changed to: "A thick face, two facades, three slogans, four seasons of clothing, five cards of poker, six acts of Peking opera, seven-word proclamations, eight rounds of mahjong, nine committee positions, and ten parts amiability." And the scope of activities has also expanded slightly with the times. For example, in the event of an accident, they issue telegrams and distribute leaflets; at gatherings, they serve as representatives and compete for committee positions; when important people come and go, they hold small flags to welcome and send them off at the dock; when wealthy people or their wives die, they handle the funeral arrangements, etc. No matter how trivial the matter, once it falls into their hands, they can do it thoroughly. These are all new tricks that the "qingke" of the past never did. Although the principle is still the old method of carrying a sign and acting as a sedan carrier.

Even those who carry signs and act as sedan carriers have times when their shoulders ache and their feet are sore, but these individuals seem to relish the things they do day and night, without feeling bored. They can truly be considered to have an extraordinary gift. Alas, is this why they are "qingke"?

Reading a Letter from Home 234

— Ya Fei

Yearning for a letter from home. Eyes piercing through. Reading a letter from home. Tears streaming down. Old mother longing. Wandering son unable to return. Dreamy soul returning to his hometown. Throwing himself into his kind mother's embrace. Asking mother what grieves her. Son also shedding tears often. Why has the son not returned for so long. Old mother's heart is not at ease. Son, don't go to singing and dancing places. Don't set foot in pleasure quarters. Mother's temples have already turned white. She will soon enter the yellow earth. Son already has a wife at home. Don't covet wild grass and idle flowers. The burden of a thousand jin already belongs to you. Several mouths are waiting to be fed. Now mother is already old. From now on, household affairs are the responsibility of the son's wife. Father left you more than ten years ago. Sleeping peacefully underground. Mother endured hardship and bitterness. Keeping watch as a young widow only for you. Son must remember mother's words. Take care of yourself while away from home. Strive to survive and move forward with determination. Don't let others stain your character. Benevolence, righteousness, propriety, wisdom, and trustworthiness. Keep them firmly in your heart. For the country and for the family, a man's ambition. Always be careful not to stray onto the wrong path. Compassionate mother, don't be sad. Son will obey mother's instructions. Being away from home for a long time, unable to return. Life's pressures are unavoidable. Leaving home for more than a year. Running around busily like an ox or a horse. Daughter-in-law at home longing for her husband to return. Son also taking care of himself while away from home. Who prepares the food and keeps me warm? Clothes torn and socks broken, I mend them myself. Letters from home arriving one after another. Only disturbing the son's mind. Lengthy words still not finished. Yellow dream is already awakened. Eyes feel swollen and painful. Tears pouring down on the pillow.

Miscellaneous Talk About Life and Death 235

— Yi Ping

Regarding the length of a person's life, I think it is not worth getting too excited about. Dying right after being born is not necessarily sad, and living to be a hundred years old is not necessarily something to celebrate. Unless you live a pig-like life of eating and sleeping, a pure soul that comes into this world, as long as you are a person, will have a net specially designed for humanity to go through, and all troubles and pains will always follow you. Those who ride in cars have the troubles and pains of riding in cars; those who pull rickshaws have the troubles and pains of pulling rickshaws. Gathering many humans of different professions and identities, rich and poor, in one room, I think this is a good lesson to study the philosophy of life.

However, people always treasure life so much. As the old saying goes, "Better to live badly than to die well," and the Bund also has the warning, "Those who die young are destined to return." The funeral music played by the bereaved family is often heartbreaking, and the words of mourning written by literati all express great sorrow for death. However, I remember what the Buddhists say, that when a person is born, his process is birth, old age, sickness, and death. Ultimately, birth is the beginning of death. So what's so surprising about living a few more years or a few less years?

The author does not have much feeling and is saying so many unrelated things because one day I went to a relative's house to celebrate his birthday and discovered the contrast between life and death. My relative did not "live" in a way that made people amazed. According to the Chinese way of calculating age, he is exactly forty years old today. Although I have heard old people say that people nowadays are not like before, and no one lives long, I have also seen a Taoist priest who is over a hundred years old in the Great World. No matter how exaggerated he is in his advertisements, he can always be proud that he is older than someone who is forty years old. My relative lived to be forty years old, and with this small record, he made a big birthday celebration, mainly to show that after he came into this world, he did not have to worry about eating and drinking. After living comfortably for forty years and having sons and grandsons, his life's mission is almost complete, so he thought it was a great joy and he can celebrate his "living" forty years, that is the meaning.

At the same time, next door to my relative, a three-year-old only son died. For the Chinese, carrying on the family line is a matter of great importance. When a man marries a wife and has a son, he can be worthy of his parents and ancestors. People often say that those with many sons have good fortune. Now that a single three-year-old son has died, that's far more tragic than a record of celebrating a fortieth birthday. Crying is inevitable. After being born, after these three years, or according to the Chinese way of calculating age, probably less than two years old. While the neighbor is telling you in loud gongs and drums that one person in his family has "lived" for forty years. Maybe ten years later, he will knock on the gongs and tell you again that the forty-year-old person has become fifty years old. With such a contrast, it is worth getting excited about living a few more years or a few less years.

The author is a twenty-five-year-old young man who does not have any great feelings about life and death. I declare early in this article that it is not written with feeling, so I hope that the relative who is celebrating his birthday and the parents of the three-year-old only son who died will not see this article. The author is just chatting casually.

Country Folk 236

— Yu Gui

One of the City Correspondences

Old friend:

If we hadn't seen your envelope at Lou's place, we wouldn't have known about your situation after three years of separation; even though we can meet anywhere in the world, I don't believe we can't see each other again.

Your letter says that in the past three years, you have been living in the countryside and have completely become a country person. Old friend, what is the difference between country people and city people? Since Heaven has created each of us as a person, and each person has Heaven within them, before we have resigned from the responsibilities that Heaven has endowed us with, we all have the same five senses and four limbs. So what is the difference between country people and city people? And after we have resigned from our responsibilities, aren't we still just a smelly leather bag?

You say, "The so-called bankruptcy of the rural economy is probably just a four-character image in the minds of urban gentlemen. The countryside is indeed in a period of economic bankruptcy, but what's the use of shouting slogans about going to the countryside? The economic bankruptcy in the countryside is just like the recession in the city. Millionaires with millions of assets will not suffer any loss no matter how bad the recession is. The situation in the countryside is exactly the same. Large farmers with thousands of acres of land live very comfortably, and all the exploitation falls on small tenant farmers who rent a few or dozens of acres from landlords..."

It is true that we, who live in the city, do not have such a perceptive understanding of the countryside. Old friend, you can rely on your own strength to cultivate your own land. If we didn't have the kind of beautiful dreams we had in school, you would probably still be happy. You can live a stable life as a country person. As for us, oppressed by the city, we cannot have that kind of happiness in this life, to live a stable life as you said. Recently, Lu lost his job. Old friend, do you know that the cost of living in Shanghai is so high that we grab a thirty-yuan job, and it's like I'm snatching it from you. It's really like you said, all the exploitation falls on us, friends who live from hand to mouth!

Lu comes to my place every day. I still have the scraps of food left over from the exploitation of the gentleman class, so when I see Lu's unemployment, I think of how my own livelihood is as precarious as a spider web. Recently, I published an article about abandoning writing and learning martial arts, wanting to take off our long robes and become members of the blue-cloth-short-shirt class, whose lives would probably be several times better than ours. However, old friend, we are surrounded by snobbish urban eyes, and our long robes maintain our forced dignity in a state of wagging our tails and begging for mercy. Old friend, would you like to come and be a city person?

Your one phrase, "country person," has stirred up many complaints. I think you would not want to receive a "country person" from the city. However, since you asked about our lives in the past three years of separation, it's really like a Twenty-Four Histories. Where to start? I think I'll slowly write you another letter.

The day before yesterday, Lu and I took a photo together. We still look like people. I'll send it to you, the country person, to see, or maybe you won't recognize us anymore. The passage of three years has aged us a lot. Old friend, this is the benefit of being a city person. If you think your body is too strong, I welcome you to come and taste the flavor of being a city person.

I'm writing this letter in the dim light. Because I wrote too much during the day, my eyes are blurry. I still want to seize the few hours of sleep I have left. Otherwise, tomorrow's bread might change. I'll stop here. I wish you a lifetime of living a stable life as a country person.

Wife's Melancholy 237

— Meng Yuan

In recent days, my wife has been a little unhappy again! Especially at night, lying in bed, thinking of her cold face, it really makes people feel an inexplicable sense of disappointment.

This is a very uninteresting thing, to be unhappy at that time; it is also the start of my writing and working. Although my body is very tired, I cannot help but cheer up and find out the reason for her unhappiness.

"Are you feeling unwell?" I asked cautiously, but she didn't answer, and even showed a more unhappy look.

This is really something only heaven knows. Being unhappy for no reason, not answering even a single question; thinking like this, I felt sad. However, getting angry is not the solution, I must be patient and ask her to make it clear.

"Baby, what's wrong? Tell me, tell your dear fellow!" I said, half showing my sincerity, half joking, coaxing her to tell the reason for her unhappiness.

But, she started crying with a "wah!"

This is really killing me! I was very angry, reminded of women's love of crying, I hate it!

"Women are really cheap things!" I was angry at this time, and felt that only by ignoring her would she live quietly.

"Hum! Yes! Women are cheap?" She spoke at this time!

Page 23

Modern Celebrity Calligraphy and Painting: Painting by Mr. Zhang Daqian from Sichuan

"People are trying to advise you and ask you nicely, how can you not make a single sound, and not pay attention to me?"

"Do you know how much I am suffering!"

"If you don't tell people what you are suffering from, how can people know?"

"How can I not have told you!" wife said loudly, accompanied by sobs.

"Clearly, you have not said a single word."

"If you say I have not said anything, then I haven't said anything." I began to think through it again from the beginning, she had indeed not said anything? So I had no choice but to remain silent and ignore her.

Strangely enough, she stopped crying like this! No, and she even started talking to me:

"I haven't had my period for two months! What if I'm pregnant?!!"

The lives of both of us still depend on our combined intelligence and labor to barely maintain; if we add another child, it will not only disrupt our forward front, but also distract us. So it is a piece of good news in wealthy families, but in our case, we are miserable!

"But, this is not something to be worried about, we are born for society, and we should not let a bad society that has not been fully reformed swallow our children; we should happily give birth to them and accelerate their cultivation to become our reserves."

At the same time, my wife also felt that this was a kind of work that women's instincts should not avoid; she smiled through her tears! But she still pointed at my forehead with her finger and said:

"You are happy, I am the one who suffers, you are really a harmful person."

She couldn't help laughing! I wanted to take the opportunity to tease her; but my mouth was covered by one of her hands!

So we smiled at each other, and she took off her clothes and went to bed. I put my arms around her and gave her a long kiss.

Twenty-Two, Eleven, Twenty-Seven, Written at night under a dim light.

A Word About "Nudity" and "Physical Fitness" 238

— Shen

| Back from Watching "Sex Education Film" |

From the major newspapers and discussions with friends who have returned from studying in Germany, I know that nude sports have already become a fashionable and popular pastime in Germany. I remember not long ago, the Shanghai fashion girls and modern young masters were also making a fuss about playing this fashionable trick, and for a while, the two venerable legs of the newspaper reporters were really busy because of this trend, and a part of the society who wanted to find new stimulation also burned their desires inwardly like crazy, wishing they could immediately take off the "chiffon" and "light silk" and other things they wore and burn them or throw them into the Huangpu River. But, this was enough to disappoint the fashion girls and modern young masters, and before it was launched, it hit a strong wall | On the wall, it was written in large characters: You "violate the law," "harm public morals," "indulge in lewdness," "exploit for profit" shameless dogs!

I myself, except when I go to bed in the bedroom at night, or when I lock the door alone and hide in the bathroom to take a bath, and take off all my clothes (Note: Nudity too), at other times, when eating, meeting guests, or going to the office, I always wear neat clothes and act as a member of the "upper-class Chinese", so, I naturally have no objection to giving those modern people who like to find new stimulation a strong wall to bump into. Moreover, I even silently thought in my mind: The advocate and implementer of this fashionable trick is the "stimulated, thirsty" fashion girls and modern young masters in this strange society | They originally had high-class clothes and precious hats, but they were tired of wearing them, annoyed by them, and bored with them, and felt a strange boredom: To break this boredom, of course, it is necessary to wear this newest and most stimulating "nude movement" | So the fashion girls and modern young masters threw away their top hats and took off their precious pants...

…………

Because of this silent thought, at that time, another trend of thought was surging and surging in my heart, pounding and causing me to feel intense pain: Let's see, let's move our gaze from the group of "girls" and "young masters" to another corner of this society, look, isn't there a big girl of eighteen years old over there who still doesn't have pants to wear? Aren't those people with yellow skin and thin bones, whose bones can be seen, already "nude" all day and all year round? Why are they "nude"? Are they looking for new stimulation because they are tired of wearing clothes, annoyed by them, and bored with them? Are they violating the law, harming public morals, indulging in lewdness, and exploiting for profit? But why are they forgiven and allowed to be free from "law" without giving them a strong wall to bump into? In this way, can we use "natural disasters" and "fate" to explain them?

Therefore, in this contradictory and confusing society, everything has some opposing sides that make it difficult to distinguish. The so-called nude movement is the same: To say that we object, indeed, we don't need to support these guys' idle games: but if we say we support it, what reason can we use to object to the "nudity" caused by "reality"?

Yesterday, after watching the sex education film "The Beauty of Women" (the film describes the rational hygiene and exercise of women in a certain country) in "Shanghai", I had many feelings in my heart. The first point is that it tells us: nude outdoor exercise can improve physical fitness (the film refers to women). The second point is that this movement is not just a trick for a few idle fashion girls and modern young masters to find new stimulation. However, how much of this is completely "ideal" for people in our strange country! Because in fact, I can't forget the eighteen-year-old girl who reportedly had no pants to wear due to "natural disasters" and "fate", and the group of people with yellow skin and thin bones who were emaciated and crying naked | Why aren't they "fit" some more with their year-round, almost habitual nudity?

Amateur Mailbox

How to Deal with a Wife? 239

Mr. Editor:

I greatly admire your newspaper's amateur advice column. I have repeatedly thought about writing to consult you, but I feared my handwriting was illegible and my writing incoherent, so I felt ashamed and dared not try. Now, my situation is becoming more urgent day by day, and I have no choice but to write to earnestly request your help in resolving it quickly. I am a clerk in a pharmacy. When I was thirteen years old, my mother arranged for me to be engaged to a Miss Wang as my wife. My father passed away early, and unexpectedly, my mother also unfortunately passed away the year before last, leaving me, this miserable child. My family is very poor. Although I aspire to be self-reliant, I cannot help but feel that one hand cannot clap alone, and my burden is becoming heavier day by day. The wedding date is also approaching. My future parents-in-law also have no sons and are both in Shanghai, leaving my fiancée to live with her married older sister. My father-in-law is now unemployed, and I also subsidize his daily expenses. Because he thinks I am young, inexperienced, and without a family head, he is now taking charge and wants to ask her to come to Shanghai to marry me. I think that although coming to Shanghai would be good, it would inevitably lead to high expenses in the future, and my salary is small, making it difficult to maintain. If I were to send her back to my hometown after the marriage, there are no relatives at home to take care of her, only unrelated neighbors, and I cannot feel at ease. This situation truly puts me in a dilemma. You, sir, are a guide for young people like us. Now, please help me think of a solution. Sincerely,

Respectfully wishing you peace,

Tong Jun

×　　×　　×　　×　　×

Editor's Note: A young man deeply involved in the world needs at least someone who shares his joys and sorrows, someone older and more experienced, as his advisor. If Mr. Tong is already an adult and can barely manage his finances, then he should adopt his father-in-law's proposal, hastily complete the wedding, and then directly and straightforwardly live with his in-laws. In case of any issues, they can discuss with each other, which is not necessarily a bad thing. Your father-in-law is currently unemployed, but this is not surprising in this recessionary era; unless he is incorrigibly evil, he will eventually find a job again. At that time, the economic aspect will no longer be a problem. He has no son, and you have no father, so it would be good to cooperate with each other. Even if he has difficulty finding a job for a while, fortunately, you are able to subsidize your future in-laws' current expenses. Setting up a separate household in Shanghai is indeed very expensive, but adding a person to the existing household will not cost much; if your wife can be hardworking and frugal, the expenses will definitely not be high. Therefore, if your future father-in-law is upright and the wedding does not cost too much, then you might as well listen to your future father-in-law's proposal.

Novel

Shanghai (8) 240

— Zhang Laosan

(15) This Scared Me

The room was silent. My cousin wanted to leave this place and was seeking my consent. Before I could speak, the sound of high heels brought in a flamboyant woman with red and white makeup on her face, which couldn't hide her faded youth. "Are all the guests here? Why haven't you gone down yet?" Her speech was as rushed as her uncle's smoking. Only then did her eyes notice me sitting at the lower end of the opium couch.

"This is your nephew," she said, always so straightforward.

My uncle nodded. My cousin pouted. Undoubtedly, she was the second wife the doorman had mentioned. I stood up and called her Aunt.

My uncle smiled triumphantly.

The second wife smiled contentedly.

"Country folk are so honest. Stay for a few days. We have empty rooms here," was the price of calling her Aunt.

"No, I'm going back soon," I replied with a reluctant smile.

My uncle had finished smoking and was adjusting his melon cap in front of the dressing mirror. "Move your luggage over. There's no need to be polite at your uncle's house." He said while still holding the extinguished cigar in his mouth.

"Hui'er..." he turned around and said, as if he had forgotten something important. He moved his body, covered with clothes, and pulled out a letter from under the ashtray and handed it to me.

"Hui'er, greet Qingping." The two mismatched figures went out the door at the same time.

The envelope only had the six characters "For Qingping, Brother" written on it. It was my younger brother's handwriting. This was the reason for my failed lie, I thought.

The footsteps on the stairs gradually disappeared. My cousin said apologetically:

"I forgot to tell you that your brother sent a quick letter. Dad was very angry when he saw it, saying that he had arrived in Shanghai on the night train the day before yesterday and forgot to see me. I heard him and said I had arranged for some classmates to come and listen to a lecture. Dad wanted me to take his car, so I gave the driver a dollar and told him to drive around. I rushed to the Qingtai Hotel where you usually stay. The clerk recognized me, but he said you hadn't come. This scared me..." She patted her chest. "I thought you weren't coming to Shanghai!"

She avoided my gaze. "Would you like to take a walk in the garden?" she changed the subject as if embarrassed.

(16) There Will Always Be Opportunities for Young People

The garden was at the back of the villa and wasn't large, but it was exquisite. Coming out of the small door behind the stairs, passing over a small bridge! The flowing water under the bridge seemed to originate from the Western-style building: a winding flower path led to a temple-like structure in the center, with three large characters "藏經樓" (Scripture Repository) hanging on it. My uncle built the villa and named it Fangwai (Beyond the World), seemingly with this intention, but he hoped to have a son.

Anxious to know what matter was worth a city girl's shyness, I had no time to appreciate the scenery of the garden and hurriedly asked, "Hui sister, what if I didn't come to Shanghai?"

"I'll tell you," she smiled. "I thought of placing an advertisement in the newspaper..."

Before she could finish, I interrupted:

"Hui sister, little brother is no longer a little brother now. If I didn't come to Shanghai, where would Shanghai go? I have friends in Shanghai, my..." I couldn't come up with a suitable Noun or Pronoun for a moment.

"Your what?" Perhaps girls have all learned the tone of mischievous children, like Min sister's "Aren't you dreaming now?" That same attitude flashed before my eyes.

I knew that perhaps a faint blush had already covered my face. I casually tore open my brother's letter. My cousin firmly grasped my wrist and said formally:

Brother, do you know, I almost didn't recognize you on the tram. You drink as much as you can. My letters to you have gone unanswered lately. Xin brother wrote to tell me that you, brother, have become like an old man. Brother, Dad doesn't like you much, but that's his temper. Wait, there will always be opportunities for you young people!

My cousin stared at me. I couldn't speak. My cousin loved me. I pitied this naturally honest country girl. Why did my mother die so early?

"Hui sister, I thank you. In short, I have already forgotten my past... Hui sister, I hope you remember, you are young too!"

She lowered her head. I was silent. The two of us walked in silence for a while. Loud laughter came from ahead. A swarm of flower butterflies, like dancing girls, flew into the garden. The one in the lead shouted loudly to my cousin: "We've been waiting for you for so long. Are you still not done talking?" She laughed, and a group of them followed suit.

"Brother, move your luggage over," Hui sister said softly and ran towards her friends.

I watched their backs disappear through the door of that Western-style building.
